<p><b>Chile</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/tʃ/: &#39;ch&#39; in &#39;China&#39;">tʃ</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Chile-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/En-Chile-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Chile-pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/tʃ/: &#39;ch&#39; in &#39;China&#39;">tʃ</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[ˈtʃile]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Chile</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:RepChile.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/50/RepChile.ogg" class="internal" title="RepChile.ogg"><span class="unicode" lang="es"><i>República de Chile</i></span></a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:RepChile.ogg" title="File:RepChile.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South American</a> country occupying a long, narrow strip of land between the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> to the east and the Pacific Ocean to the west. It borders <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> to the east, and the <a href="/wiki/Drake_Passage" title="Drake Passage">Drake Passage</a> in the far south. Chilean territory includes the Pacific islands of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Fern%C3%A1ndez_Islands" title="Juan Fernández Islands">Juan Fernández</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salas_y_G%C3%B3mez" class="mw-redirect" title="Salas y Gómez">Salas y Gómez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desventuradas_Islands" title="Desventuradas Islands">Desventuradas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>. Chile also claims about 1,250,000 square kilometres (480,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>, although all claims are suspended under the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Antarctic Treaty">Antarctic Treaty</a>.
</p><p>The arid <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a> in northern Chile contains great mineral wealth, principally <a href="/wiki/Copper#Production" title="Copper">copper</a> and lithium. The relatively small central area dominates in terms of population and agricultural resources, and is the cultural and political center from which Chile expanded in the late 19th century when it incorporated its northern and southern regions. Southern Chile is rich in forests and grazing lands, and features a string of <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a> and lakes. The southern coast is a labyrinth of <a href="/wiki/Fjords_and_channels_of_Chile" title="Fjords and channels of Chile">fjords, inlets, canals</a>, twisting peninsulas, and islands.<sup id="cite_ref-USDoS_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDoS-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Chile" title="Conquest of Chile">Spain conquered and colonized</a> the region in the mid-16th century, replacing <a href="/wiki/Incas_in_Central_Chile" title="Incas in Central Chile">Inca rule</a> in the north and centre, but <a href="/wiki/Arauco_War" title="Arauco War">failing to conquer</a> the independent <a href="/wiki/Mapuche" title="Mapuche">Mapuche</a> who inhabited what is now south-central Chile. After <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Chilean Declaration of Independence">declaring its independence</a> from Spain in 1818, Chile emerged in the 1830s as a relatively stable authoritarian republic. In the 19th century, Chile saw significant economic and territorial growth, <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Araucan%C3%ADa" title="Occupation of Araucanía">ending Mapuche resistance</a> in the 1880s and gaining its current northern territory in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> (1879–83) after defeating Peru and Bolivia.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In the 1960s and 1970s, the country experienced severe left-right <a href="/wiki/Polarization_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Polarization (politics)">political polarization</a> and turmoil. This development culminated with the <a href="/wiki/1973_Chilean_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1973 Chilean coup d&#39;état">1973 Chilean coup d'état</a> that overthrew <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Allende" title="Salvador Allende">Salvador Allende</a>'s democratically elected left-wing government and instituted <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship_of_Chile_(1973%E2%80%9390)" class="mw-redirect" title="Military dictatorship of Chile (1973–90)">a 16-year-long right-wing military dictatorship</a> that left more than 3,000 people dead or missing.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Chile_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Chile-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The regime, headed by <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet</a>, ended in 1990 after it lost a <a href="/wiki/Chilean_presidential_referendum,_1988" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilean presidential referendum, 1988">referendum in 1988</a> and was succeeded by a <a href="/wiki/Concertaci%C3%B3n" title="Concertación">center-left coalition</a> which ruled through four presidencies until 2010.
</p><p>The modern <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Chile is among South America's most economically and socially stable and prosperous nations, with a <a href="/wiki/High-income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High-income economy">high-income economy</a> and high <a href="/wiki/Living_standards" class="mw-redirect" title="Living standards">living standards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Chile_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Chile-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> It leads <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin American</a> nations in rankings of <a href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Human development (humanity)">human development</a>, <a href="/wiki/Competition_(companies)" title="Competition (companies)">competitiveness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Income_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="Income per capita">income per capita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">state of peace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">economic freedom</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">low perception of corruption</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> It also ranks high regionally in <a href="/wiki/Failed_States_Index#Failed_States_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Failed States Index">sustainability of the state</a>, and democratic development.<sup id="cite_ref-wdi_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wdi-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Chile is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD), joining in 2010. Currently it also has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">lowest homicide rate in the Americas after Canada</a>. Chile is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a> (UNASUR), the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a> (CELAC) and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Alliance" title="Pacific Alliance">Pacific Alliance</a>.
</p>
