</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>There are various theories about the origin of the word <i>Chile</i>. According to 17th-century Spanish chronicler <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Rosales" title="Diego de Rosales">Diego de Rosales</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Incas" class="mw-redirect" title="Incas">Incas</a> called the valley of the <a href="/wiki/Aconcagua" title="Aconcagua">Aconcagua</a> "Chili" by corruption of the name of a <a href="/wiki/Picunche" title="Picunche">Picunche</a> <a href="/wiki/Tribal_chief" title="Tribal chief">tribal chief</a> ("cacique") called <i>Tili</i>, who ruled the area at the time of the Incan conquest in the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-encina_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encina-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Another theory points to the similarity of the valley of the Aconcagua with that of the <a href="/wiki/Casma_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Casma Valley">Casma Valley</a> in Peru, where there was a town and valley named <i>Chili</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-encina_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encina-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other theories say Chile may derive its name from a <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a> word meaning either "ends of the earth" or "sea gulls";<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> from the Mapuche word <i>chilli,</i> which may mean "where the land ends;"<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> or from the <a href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a> <i>chiri</i>, "cold",<sup id="cite_ref-1911britannica_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1911britannica-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> or <i>tchili</i>, meaning either "snow"<sup id="cite_ref-1911britannica_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1911britannica-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> or "the deepest point of the Earth".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Another origin attributed to <i>chilli</i> is the onomatopoeic <i>cheele-cheele</i>—the Mapuche imitation of the warble of a bird locally known as <a href="/wiki/Yellow-winged_blackbird" title="Yellow-winged blackbird">trile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistadors" class="mw-redirect" title="Conquistadors">conquistadors</a> heard about this name from the Incas, and the few survivors of <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Almagro" title="Diego de Almagro">Diego de Almagro</a>'s first Spanish expedition south from Peru in 1535–36 called themselves the "men of Chilli".<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Ultimately, Almagro is credited with the universalization of the name <i>Chile</i>, after naming the <a href="/wiki/Mapocho_River" title="Mapocho River">Mapocho</a> valley as such.<sup id="cite_ref-encina_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encina-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The older spelling "Chili" was in use in English until at least 1900 before switching to "Chile".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Chile" title="History of Chile">History of Chile</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>
<p>Stone tool evidence indicates humans sporadically frequented the <a href="/wiki/Monte_Verde" title="Monte Verde">Monte Verde</a> valley area as long as 18,500 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> About 10,000 years ago, migrating <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Peoples_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous Peoples of the Americas">indigenous Peoples</a> settled in fertile valleys and coastal areas of what is present-day Chile. Settlement sites from very early human habitation include Monte Verde, <a href="/wiki/Cueva_del_Milod%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Cueva del Milodón">Cueva del Milodón</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pali-Aike_Crater" class="mw-redirect" title="Pali-Aike Crater">Pali-Aike Crater</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Lava_tube" title="Lava tube">lava tube</a>. The Incas briefly extended their empire into what is now northern Chile, but the <a href="/wiki/Mapuche" title="Mapuche">Mapuche</a> (or Araucanians as they were known by the Spaniards) successfully resisted many attempts by the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a> to subjugate them, despite their lack of state organization.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> They fought against the Sapa Inca Tupac Yupanqui and his army. The result of the bloody three-day confrontation known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Maule" title="Battle of the Maule">Battle of the Maule</a> was that the Inca conquest of the territories of Chile ended at the <a href="/wiki/Maule_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Maule river">Maule river</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_colonization">Spanish colonization</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Chile" title="Conquest of Chile">Conquest of Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Chile" title="Colonial Chile">Colonial Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lautaro_(de_Pedro_Subercaseaux).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Lautaro_%28de_Pedro_Subercaseaux%29.jpg/150px-Lautaro_%28de_Pedro_Subercaseaux%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Lautaro_%28de_Pedro_Subercaseaux%29.jpg/225px-Lautaro_%28de_Pedro_Subercaseaux%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Lautaro_%28de_Pedro_Subercaseaux%29.jpg/300px-Lautaro_%28de_Pedro_Subercaseaux%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1007" data-file-height="1614" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lautaro_(de_Pedro_Subercaseaux).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lautaro" title="Lautaro">Lautaro</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Toqui" title="Toqui">toqui</a></i> and hero of the <a href="/wiki/Arauco_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Arauco war">Arauco war</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1520, while attempting to circumnavigate the globe, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> discovered the southern passage now named after him (the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">Strait of Magellan</a>) thus becoming the first European to set foot on what is now Chile. The next Europeans to reach Chile were Diego de Almagro and his band of <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">Spanish conquistadors</a>, who came from <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> in 1535 seeking gold. The Spanish encountered various cultures that supported themselves principally through <a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">slash-and-burn</a> agriculture and hunting.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_de_Valdivia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Pedro_de_Valdivia.jpg/150px-Pedro_de_Valdivia.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Pedro_de_Valdivia.jpg/225px-Pedro_de_Valdivia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Pedro_de_Valdivia.jpg/300px-Pedro_de_Valdivia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="615" data-file-height="790" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_de_Valdivia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Valdivia" title="Pedro de Valdivia">Pedro de Valdivia</a>, conqueror of Chile</div></div></div>
<p>The conquest of Chile began in earnest in 1540 and was carried out by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Valdivia" title="Pedro de Valdivia">Pedro de Valdivia</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pizarro" title="Francisco Pizarro">Francisco Pizarro</a>'s lieutenants, who founded the city of Santiago on 12 February 1541. Although the Spanish did not find the extensive gold and silver they sought, they recognized the agricultural potential of Chile's central valley, and Chile became part of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Conquest took place gradually, and the Europeans suffered repeated setbacks. A massive <a href="/wiki/Mapuche" title="Mapuche">Mapuche</a> insurrection that began in 1553 resulted in Valdivia's death and the destruction of many of the colony's principal settlements. Subsequent major insurrections took place in 1598 and in 1655. Each time the Mapuche and other native groups revolted, the southern border of the colony was driven northward. The abolition of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> by the Spanish crown in 1683 was done in recognition that enslaving the Mapuche intensified resistance rather than cowing them into submission. Despite royal prohibitions, relations remained strained from continual colonialist interference.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cut off to the north by desert, to the south by the Mapuche, to the east by the Andes Mountains, and to the west by the ocean, Chile became one of the most centralized, homogeneous colonies in Spanish America. Serving as a sort of frontier <a href="/wiki/Garrison" title="Garrison">garrison</a>, the colony found itself with the mission of forestalling encroachment by both the Mapuche and Spain's European enemies, especially the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> and the Dutch. Buccaneers and English adventurers menaced the colony in addition to the Mapuche, as was shown by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Francis_Drake" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Francis Drake">Sir Francis Drake</a>'s 1578 raid on Valparaíso, the colony's principal port. Chile hosted one of the largest standing armies in the Americas, making it one of the most militarized of the Spanish possessions, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Real_Situado" title="Real Situado">drain on the treasury of the Viceroyalty of Peru</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first general census was conducted by the government of <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_de_J%C3%A1uregui" title="Agustín de Jáuregui">Agustín de Jáuregui</a> between 1777 and 1778; it indicated that the population consisted of 259,646 inhabitants: 73.5 percent of <a href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White Latin American">European descent</a>, 7.9 percent <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a>, 8.6 percent <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples</a> and 9.8 percent blacks. Francisco Hurtado, Governor of the province of <a href="/wiki/Chilo%C3%A9_Province" title="Chiloé Province">Chiloé</a>, conducted a census in 1784 and found the population consisted of 26,703 inhabitants, 64.4 percent of whom were whites and 33.5 percent of whom were natives.
</p><p>The Diocese of <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n,_Chile" title="Concepción, Chile">Concepción</a> conducted a census in areas south of the <a href="/wiki/Maule_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Maule river">Maule river</a> in 1812, but did not include the indigenous population or the inhabitants of the province of Chiloé. The population is estimated at 210,567, 86.1 percent of whom were <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Chilean" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Chilean">Spanish</a> or of European descent, 10 percent of whom were indigenous and 3.7 percent of whom were mestizos, blacks and <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">mulattos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_nation_building">Independence and nation building</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chilean_War_of_Independence" title="Chilean War of Independence">Chilean War of Independence</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Argentine%E2%80%93Chilean_naval_arms_race" title="Argentine–Chilean naval arms race">Argentine–Chilean naval arms race</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohiggins.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ohiggins.jpg/200px-Ohiggins.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ohiggins.jpg/300px-Ohiggins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ohiggins.jpg/400px-Ohiggins.jpg 2x" data-file-width="852" data-file-height="1087" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohiggins.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bernardo_O%27Higgins" title="Bernardo O&#39;Higgins">Bernardo O'Higgins</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Libertadores" title="Libertadores">Libertador</a></i> and the Supreme Director of Chile</div></div></div>
<p>In 1808, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I">Napoleon's</a> enthronement of his brother <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish monarchy">Spanish King</a> precipitated the drive by the colony for <a href="/wiki/Chilean_War_of_Independence" title="Chilean War of Independence">independence from Spain</a>. A national <a href="/wiki/Junta_(governing_body)" title="Junta (governing body)">junta</a> in the name of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand</a> – heir to the deposed king – was formed on 18 September 1810. The <a href="/wiki/Government_Junta_of_Chile_(1810)" title="Government Junta of Chile (1810)">Government Junta of Chile</a> proclaimed Chile an autonomous republic within the Spanish monarchy (in memory of this day, Chile celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_Patrias_(Chile)" title="Fiestas Patrias (Chile)">National Day</a> on 18 September each year).
</p><p>After these events, a movement for total independence, under the command of <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Carrera" title="José Miguel Carrera">José Miguel Carrera</a> (one of the most renowned patriots) and his two brothers Juan José and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Carrera" title="Luis Carrera">Luis Carrera</a>, soon gained a wider following. Spanish attempts to re-impose arbitrary rule during what was called the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista_(Spanish_America)" title="Reconquista (Spanish America)">Reconquista</a> led to a prolonged struggle, including infighting from <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_O%27Higgins" title="Bernardo O&#39;Higgins">Bernardo O'Higgins</a>, who challenged Carrera's leadership.
</p><p>Intermittent warfare continued until 1817. With Carrera in prison in Argentina, O'Higgins and anti-Carrera cohort <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">José de San Martín</a>, hero of the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_War_of_Independence" title="Argentine War of Independence">Argentine War of Independence</a>, led <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Andes" title="Army of the Andes">an army</a> that <a href="/wiki/Crossing_of_the_Andes" title="Crossing of the Andes">crossed the Andes</a> into Chile and defeated the royalists. On 12 February 1818, <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Chilean Declaration of Independence">Chile was proclaimed an independent republic</a>. The political revolt brought little social change, however, and 19th-century Chilean society preserved the essence of the stratified colonial social structure, which was greatly influenced by family politics and the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>. A strong presidency eventually emerged, but wealthy landowners remained powerful.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile slowly started to expand its influence and to establish its borders. By the Tantauco Treaty, the archipelago of Chiloé was incorporated in 1826. The economy began to boom due to the discovery of silver ore in Chañarcillo, and the growing trade of the port of Valparaíso, which led to conflict over maritime supremacy in the Pacific with Peru. At the same time, attempts were made to strengthen sovereignty in southern Chile intensifying <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Araucan%C3%ADa" title="Occupation of Araucanía">penetration into Araucanía</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_colonization_of_Valdivia,_Osorno_and_Llanquihue" title="German colonization of Valdivia, Osorno and Llanquihue">colonizing Llanquihue with German immigrants</a> in 1848. Through the founding of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bulnes" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Bulnes">Fort Bulnes</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Schooner_Ancud" class="mw-redirect" title="Schooner Ancud">Schooner Ancud</a> under the command of <a href="/wiki/John_Williams_Wilson" title="John Williams Wilson">John Williams Wilson</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Magallanes_Region" title="Magallanes Region">Magallanes region</a> joined the country in 1843, while the <a href="/wiki/Antofagasta_Region" title="Antofagasta Region">Antofagasta region</a>, at the time part of Bolivia, began to fill with people.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinking_of_the_Esmeralda_during_the_battle_of_Iquique.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Sinking_of_the_Esmeralda_during_the_battle_of_Iquique.jpg/250px-Sinking_of_the_Esmeralda_during_the_battle_of_Iquique.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Sinking_of_the_Esmeralda_during_the_battle_of_Iquique.jpg/375px-Sinking_of_the_Esmeralda_during_the_battle_of_Iquique.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Sinking_of_the_Esmeralda_during_the_battle_of_Iquique.jpg/500px-Sinking_of_the_Esmeralda_during_the_battle_of_Iquique.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1163" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinking_of_the_Esmeralda_during_the_battle_of_Iquique.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Iquique" title="Battle of Iquique">Battle of Iquique</a> on 21 May 1879. The victory of Chile in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> allowed its expansion into new territories.</div></div></div>
<p>Toward the end of the 19th century, the government in Santiago consolidated its position in the south by the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Araucan%C3%ADa" title="Occupation of Araucanía">Occupation of Araucanía</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boundary_treaty_of_1881_between_Chile_and_Argentina" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary treaty of 1881 between Chile and Argentina">Boundary treaty of 1881 between Chile and Argentina</a> confirmed Chilean sovereignty over the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">Strait of Magellan</a>. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> with Peru and Bolivia (1879–83), Chile expanded its territory northward by almost one-third, eliminating Bolivia's access to the Pacific, and acquired valuable <a href="/wiki/Caliche_(mineral)#Chilean_caliche" class="mw-redirect" title="Caliche (mineral)">nitrate</a> deposits, the exploitation of which led to an era of national affluence. Chile had joined the stand as one of the high-income countries in South America by 1870.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1891_Chilean_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="1891 Chilean Civil War">1891 Chilean Civil War</a> brought about a redistribution of power between the President and Congress, and Chile established a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> style democracy. However, the Civil War had also been a contest between those who favored the development of local industries and powerful Chilean banking interests, particularly the House of Edwards who had strong ties to foreign investors. Soon after, the country engaged in a <a href="/wiki/Argentine%E2%80%93Chilean_naval_arms_race" title="Argentine–Chilean naval arms race">vastly expensive naval arms race</a> with <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> that nearly led to war.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Era_in_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary Era in Chile">Parliamentary Era in Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/1960_Valdivia_earthquake" title="1960 Valdivia earthquake">1960 Valdivia earthquake</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_American_dreadnought_race" title="South American dreadnought race">South American dreadnought race</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chilean_battleship_Almirante_Latorre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Chilean_battleship_Almirante_Latorre.jpg/250px-Chilean_battleship_Almirante_Latorre.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Chilean_battleship_Almirante_Latorre.jpg/375px-Chilean_battleship_Almirante_Latorre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Chilean_battleship_Almirante_Latorre.jpg/500px-Chilean_battleship_Almirante_Latorre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3612" data-file-height="2236" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chilean_battleship_Almirante_Latorre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chile's <i>Almirante Latorre</i> <a href="/wiki/Dreadnought" title="Dreadnought">dreadnought</a> in 1921</div></div></div>
<p>The Chilean economy partially degenerated into a system protecting the interests of a ruling <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchy</a>. By the 1920s, the emerging middle and working classes were powerful enough to elect a reformist president, <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Alessandri" title="Arturo Alessandri">Arturo Alessandri</a>, whose program was frustrated by a conservative congress. In the 1920s, <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a> groups with strong popular support arose.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A military coup led by General <a href="/wiki/Luis_Altamirano" title="Luis Altamirano">Luis Altamirano</a> in 1924 set off a period of political instability that lasted until 1932. Of the ten governments that held power in that period, the longest lasting was that of General <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Ib%C3%A1%C3%B1ez_del_Campo" title="Carlos Ibáñez del Campo">Carlos Ibáñez del Campo</a>, who briefly held power in 1925 and then again between 1927 and 1931 in what was a <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> dictatorship (although not really comparable in harshness or corruption to the type of military dictatorship that has often bedeviled the rest of Latin America).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By relinquishing power to a democratically elected successor, Ibáñez del Campo retained the respect of a large enough segment of the population to remain a viable politician for more than thirty years, in spite of the vague and shifting nature of his ideology. When constitutional rule was restored in 1932, a strong middle-class party, the Radicals, emerged. It became the key force in coalition governments for the next 20 years. During the period of <a href="/wiki/Radical_Party_(Chile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Radical Party (Chile)">Radical Party</a> dominance (1932–52), the state increased its role in the economy. In 1952, voters returned Ibáñez del Campo to office for another six years. <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Alessandri" title="Jorge Alessandri">Jorge Alessandri</a> succeeded Ibáñez del Campo in 1958, bringing Chilean conservatism back into power democratically for another term.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1964_Chilean_presidential_election" title="1964 Chilean presidential election">1964 presidential election</a> of <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democrat_Party_of_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democrat Party of Chile">Christian Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Frei_Montalva" title="Eduardo Frei Montalva">Eduardo Frei Montalva</a> by an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_majority" class="mw-redirect" title="Absolute majority">absolute majority</a> initiated a period of major reform. Under the slogan "Revolution in Liberty", the Frei administration embarked on far-reaching social and economic programs, particularly in education, housing, and <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_reform" title="Agrarian reform">agrarian reform</a>, including rural unionization of agricultural workers. By 1967, however, Frei encountered increasing opposition from leftists, who charged that his reforms were inadequate, and from conservatives, who found them excessive. At the end of his term, Frei had not fully achieved his party's ambitious goals.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salvador_Allende_Gossens-.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Salvador_Allende_Gossens-.jpg/190px-Salvador_Allende_Gossens-.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Salvador_Allende_Gossens-.jpg/285px-Salvador_Allende_Gossens-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0d/Salvador_Allende_Gossens-.jpg 2x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="421" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salvador_Allende_Gossens-.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Salvador_Allende" title="Salvador Allende">Salvador Allende</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the 1970 election, Senator <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Allende" title="Salvador Allende">Salvador Allende</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Chile" title="Socialist Party of Chile">Socialist Party of Chile</a> (then part of the "<a href="/wiki/Popular_Unity_(Chile)" title="Popular Unity (Chile)">Popular Unity</a>" coalition which included the Communists, Radicals, Social-Democrats, dissident Christian Democrats, the Popular Unitary Action Movement, and the Independent Popular Action),<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> achieved a partial majority in a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a> of votes in a three-way contest, followed by candidates Radomiro Tomic for the Christian Democrat Party and Jorge Alessandri for the Conservative Party. Allende was not elected with an absolute majority, receiving fewer than 35 percent of votes.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Chile" title="National Congress of Chile">Chilean Congress</a> conducted a runoff vote between the leading candidates, Allende and former president Jorge Alessandri, and, keeping with tradition, chose Allende by a vote of 153 to 35. Frei refused to form an alliance with Alessandri to oppose Allende, on the grounds that the Christian Democrats were a workers' party and could not make common cause with the right wing.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Economic_depression" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic depression">economic depression</a> that began in 1972 was exacerbated by <a href="/wiki/Capital_flight" title="Capital flight">capital flight</a>, plummeting private investment, and withdrawal of bank deposits in response to Allende's socialist program. Production fell and unemployment rose. Allende adopted measures including price freezes, wage increases, and tax reforms, to increase consumer spending and redistribute income downward.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Joint public-private <a href="/wiki/Public_works" title="Public works">public works</a> projects helped reduce unemployment.<sup id="cite_ref-De_Vylder_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Vylder-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2010)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Much of the banking sector was <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalized</a>. Many enterprises within the <a href="/wiki/Copper#Production" title="Copper">copper</a>, coal, iron, <a href="/wiki/Caliche_(mineral)#Chilean_caliche" class="mw-redirect" title="Caliche (mineral)">nitrate</a>, and steel industries were <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">expropriated</a>, nationalized, or subjected to state intervention. Industrial output increased sharply and unemployment fell during the Allende administration's first year.<sup id="cite_ref-De_Vylder_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Vylder-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allende's program included advancement of workers' interests,<sup id="cite_ref-De_Vylder_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Vylder-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> replacing the judicial system with "socialist legality",<sup id="cite_ref-friedman368_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedman368-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> nationalization of banks and forcing others to bankruptcy,<sup id="cite_ref-friedman368_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedman368-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and strengthening "popular militias" known as MIR.<sup id="cite_ref-friedman368_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedman368-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Started under former President Frei, the Popular Unity platform also called for nationalization of Chile's major copper mines in the form of a constitutional amendment. The measure was passed unanimously by Congress.
</p><p>As a result,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> administration <a href="/wiki/United_States_intervention_in_Chile" title="United States intervention in Chile">organized and inserted secret operatives</a> in Chile, in order to swiftly destabilize Allende's government.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In addition, US financial pressure restricted international economic credit to Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-fas.org_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fas.org-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The economic problems were also exacerbated by Allende's public spending which was financed mostly by printing money and poor credit ratings given by commercial banks.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
Simultaneously, opposition media, politicians, business guilds and other organizations helped to accelerate a campaign of domestic political and economical destabilization, some of which was backed by the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-fas.org_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fas.org-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> By early 1973, inflation was out of control. The crippled economy was further battered by prolonged and sometimes simultaneous strikes by physicians, teachers, students, truck owners, copper workers, and the small business class.
On 26 May 1973, Chile's Supreme Court, which was opposed to Allende's government, unanimously denounced the Allende <i>disruption of the legality of the nation</i>. Although illegal under the Chilean constitution, the court supported and strengthened Pinochet's soon-to-be seizure of power.<sup id="cite_ref-friedman368_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedman368-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Pinochet_era_.281973.E2.80.931990.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pinochet_era_(1973–1990)">Pinochet era (1973–1990)</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Military_government_of_Chile_(1973%E2%80%9390)" class="mw-redirect" title="Military government of Chile (1973–90)">Military government of Chile (1973–90)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miracle_of_Chile" title="Miracle of Chile">Miracle of Chile</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Beagle_conflict" title="Beagle conflict">Beagle conflict</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Golpe_de_Estado_1973.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Golpe_de_Estado_1973.jpg/200px-Golpe_de_Estado_1973.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Golpe_de_Estado_1973.jpg/300px-Golpe_de_Estado_1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Golpe_de_Estado_1973.jpg/400px-Golpe_de_Estado_1973.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Golpe_de_Estado_1973.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">Fighter jets</a> bombing the Presidential Palace of <i>La Moneda</i> during the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_coup_of_1973" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilean coup of 1973">Chilean coup of 1973</a></div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Chilean_coup_of_1973" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilean coup of 1973">military coup</a> overthrew Allende on 11 September 1973. As the armed forces bombarded the <a href="/wiki/La_Moneda_Palace" title="La Moneda Palace">presidential palace</a>, Allende apparently committed suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> After the coup, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">Henry Kissinger</a> told <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. president</a> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> that the United States had "helped" the coup.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A military junta, led by General <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet</a>, took control of the country. The first years of the regime were marked by <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations_in_Pinochet%27s_Chile" title="Human rights violations in Pinochet&#39;s Chile">human rights violations</a>. Chile actively participated in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On October 1973, at least 72 people were murdered by the <a href="/wiki/Caravan_of_Death" title="Caravan of Death">Caravan of Death</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Rettig_Report" title="Rettig Report">Rettig Report</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valech_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Valech Commission">Valech Commission</a>, at least 2,115 were killed,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and at least 27,265<sup id="cite_ref-sintesis_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sintesis-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> were tortured (including 88 children younger than 12 years old).<sup id="cite_ref-sintesis_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sintesis-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Chile recognized an additional 9,800 victims, bringing the total number of killed, tortured or imprisoned for political reasons to 40,018.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> At the national stadium, filled with detainees, one of those tortured and killed was internationally known poet-singer <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Jara" title="Víctor Jara">Víctor Jara</a> (see "Music and Dance", below). The stadium was renamed for Jara in 2003.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Augusto_Pinochet_foto_oficial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Augusto_Pinochet_foto_oficial.jpg/200px-Augusto_Pinochet_foto_oficial.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Augusto_Pinochet_foto_oficial.jpg/300px-Augusto_Pinochet_foto_oficial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Augusto_Pinochet_foto_oficial.jpg/400px-Augusto_Pinochet_foto_oficial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="509" data-file-height="708" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Augusto_Pinochet_foto_oficial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet</a></div></div></div>
<p>A new Constitution was approved by a controversial <a href="/wiki/Plebiscite" class="mw-redirect" title="Plebiscite">plebiscite</a> on 11 September 1980, and General Pinochet became president of the republic for an eight-year term. After Pinochet obtained rule of the country, several hundred committed Chilean revolutionaries joined the <a href="/wiki/Sandinista" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandinista">Sandinista</a> army in <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, guerrilla forces in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> or training camps in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, Eastern Europe and Northern Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the late 1980s, largely as a result of events such as the 1982 economic collapse<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and mass <a href="/wiki/Civil_resistance" title="Civil resistance">civil resistance</a> in 1983–88, the government gradually permitted greater freedom of assembly, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">speech</a>, and association, to include trade union and political activity.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The government launched market-oriented reforms with <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_B%C3%BCchi" title="Hernán Büchi">Hernán Büchi</a> as Minister of Finance. Chile moved toward a <a href="/wiki/Free_market_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Free market economy">free market economy</a> that saw an increase in domestic and foreign private investment, although the <a href="/wiki/Copper#Production" title="Copper">copper</a> industry and other important mineral resources were not opened for competition. In a <a href="/wiki/1988_Chilean_national_plebiscite" title="1988 Chilean national plebiscite">plebiscite</a> on 5 October 1988, Pinochet was denied a second eight-year term as president (56% against 44%). Chileans elected a new president and the majority of members of a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> congress on 14 December 1989. Christian Democrat <a href="/wiki/Patricio_Aylwin" title="Patricio Aylwin">Patricio Aylwin</a>, the candidate of a coalition of 17 political parties called the <i><a href="/wiki/Concertaci%C3%B3n" title="Concertación">Concertación</a></i>, received an absolute majority of votes (55%).<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> President Aylwin served from 1990 to 1994, in what was considered a transition period.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2010_Chile_earthquake" title="2010 Chile earthquake">2010 Chile earthquake</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Izamiento_de_la_Gran_Bandera_Nacional_-_Presidentes_de_Chile.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Izamiento_de_la_Gran_Bandera_Nacional_-_Presidentes_de_Chile.jpg/230px-Izamiento_de_la_Gran_Bandera_Nacional_-_Presidentes_de_Chile.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Izamiento_de_la_Gran_Bandera_Nacional_-_Presidentes_de_Chile.jpg/345px-Izamiento_de_la_Gran_Bandera_Nacional_-_Presidentes_de_Chile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Izamiento_de_la_Gran_Bandera_Nacional_-_Presidentes_de_Chile.jpg/460px-Izamiento_de_la_Gran_Bandera_Nacional_-_Presidentes_de_Chile.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1606" data-file-height="1111" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Izamiento_de_la_Gran_Bandera_Nacional_-_Presidentes_de_Chile.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Five presidents of Chile since <a href="/wiki/Transition_to_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Transition to democracy">Transition to democracy</a> (1990–2018), celebrating the <a href="/wiki/Bicentennial_of_Chile" title="Bicentennial of Chile">Bicentennial of Chile</a></div></div></div>
<p>In December 1993, Christian Democrat <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Frei_Ruiz-Tagle" title="Eduardo Frei Ruiz-Tagle">Eduardo Frei Ruiz-Tagle</a>, the son of previous president Eduardo Frei Montalva, led the Concertación coalition to victory with an absolute majority of votes (58%).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Frei Ruiz-Tagle was succeeded in 2000 by Socialist <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lagos" title="Ricardo Lagos">Ricardo Lagos</a>, who won the presidency in an unprecedented <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Chilean_presidential_election" title="2009–10 Chilean presidential election">runoff election</a> against <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Lav%C3%ADn" title="Joaquín Lavín">Joaquín Lavín</a> of the rightist <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance for Chile">Alliance for Chile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In January 2006, Chileans elected their first female president, <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet_Jeria" class="mw-redirect" title="Michelle Bachelet Jeria">Michelle Bachelet Jeria</a>, of the Socialist Party, defeating <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Pi%C3%B1era" title="Sebastián Piñera">Sebastián Piñera</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/National_Renewal_(Chile)" title="National Renewal (Chile)">National Renewal</a> party, extending the <i>Concertación</i> governance for another four years.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In January 2010, Chileans <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Chilean_presidential_election" title="2009–10 Chilean presidential election">elected</a> <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Pi%C3%B1era" title="Sebastián Piñera">Sebastián Piñera</a> as the first rightist President in 20 years, defeating former President <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Frei_Ruiz-Tagle" title="Eduardo Frei Ruiz-Tagle">Eduardo Frei Ruiz-Tagle</a> of the <i>Concertación</i>, for a four-year term succeeding Bachelet. Due to term limits, <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Pi%C3%B1era" title="Sebastián Piñera">Sebastián Piñera</a> did not stand for re-election in 2013, and his term expired in March 2014 resulting in <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet" title="Michelle Bachelet">Michelle Bachelet</a> returning to office.
</p><p>On 27 February 2010, Chile was struck by an 8.8 <a href="/wiki/Seismic_magnitude_scales#Mw" title="Seismic magnitude scales"><span title="Moment mag. scale">M<sub>w</sub></span></a> <a href="/wiki/2010_Chile_earthquake" title="2010 Chile earthquake">earthquake</a>, the fifth largest ever recorded at the time. More than 500 people died (most from the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a>) and over a million people lost their homes. The earthquake was also followed by multiple aftershocks.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Initial damage estimates were in the range of US$15–30 billion, around 10 to 15 percent of Chile's real gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile achieved global recognition for the successful <a href="/wiki/2010_Copiap%C3%B3_mining_accident" title="2010 Copiapó mining accident">rescue of 33 trapped miners</a> in 2010. On 5 August 2010 the access tunnel collapsed at the San José copper and gold mine in the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a> near <a href="/wiki/Copiap%C3%B3" title="Copiapó">Copiapó</a> in northern Chile, trapping 33 men 700 metres (2,300&#160;ft) below ground. A rescue effort organized by the Chilean government located the miners 17 days later. All 33 men were brought to the surface two months later on 13 October 2010 over a period of almost 24 hours, an effort that was carried on live television around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-usstatedep_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usstatedep-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Chile" title="Politics of Chile">Politics of Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Chile" title="Law of Chile">Law of Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_la_Moneda_desde_Plaza_de_la_Constituci%C3%B3n.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Palacio_de_la_Moneda_desde_Plaza_de_la_Constituci%C3%B3n.jpg/220px-Palacio_de_la_Moneda_desde_Plaza_de_la_Constituci%C3%B3n.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Palacio_de_la_Moneda_desde_Plaza_de_la_Constituci%C3%B3n.jpg/330px-Palacio_de_la_Moneda_desde_Plaza_de_la_Constituci%C3%B3n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Palacio_de_la_Moneda_desde_Plaza_de_la_Constituci%C3%B3n.jpg/440px-Palacio_de_la_Moneda_desde_Plaza_de_la_Constituci%C3%B3n.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3040" data-file-height="2016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_la_Moneda_desde_Plaza_de_la_Constituci%C3%B3n.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_La_Moneda" class="mw-redirect" title="Palacio de La Moneda">Palacio de La Moneda</a> in downtown <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago, Chile">Santiago</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:181px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_Santiago_de_Chile_-_Fachada_del_edificio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/2017_Santiago_de_Chile_-_Fachada_del_edificio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia.jpg/179px-2017_Santiago_de_Chile_-_Fachada_del_edificio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia.jpg" decoding="async" width="179" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/2017_Santiago_de_Chile_-_Fachada_del_edificio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia.jpg/269px-2017_Santiago_de_Chile_-_Fachada_del_edificio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/2017_Santiago_de_Chile_-_Fachada_del_edificio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia.jpg/358px-2017_Santiago_de_Chile_-_Fachada_del_edificio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3801" data-file-height="5067" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_Santiago_de_Chile_-_Fachada_del_edificio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_los_Tribunales_de_Justicia_de_Santiago" title="Palacio de los Tribunales de Justicia de Santiago">Palace of Justice</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a></div></div></div>
<p>The current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Chile" title="Constitution of Chile">Constitution of Chile</a> was approved in a national <a href="/wiki/Plebiscite" class="mw-redirect" title="Plebiscite">plebiscite</a>—regarded as "highly irregular" by some observers<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>—in September 1980, under the military government of Augusto Pinochet. It entered into force in March 1981. After Pinochet's defeat in the <a href="/wiki/1988_Chilean_national_plebiscite" title="1988 Chilean national plebiscite">1988 plebiscite</a>, the constitution was amended to ease provisions for future amendments to the Constitution. In September 2005, President Ricardo Lagos signed into law several constitutional amendments passed by Congress. These include eliminating the positions of appointed senators and <a href="/wiki/Senators_for_life" class="mw-redirect" title="Senators for life">senators for life</a>, granting the President authority to remove the commanders-in-chief of the armed forces, and reducing the presidential term from six to four years.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Congress of Chile">Congress of Chile</a> has a 38-seat <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Chile" title="Senate of Chile">Senate</a> and a 120-member <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Chile" title="Chamber of Deputies of Chile">Chamber of Deputies</a>. Senators serve for eight years with staggered terms, while deputies are elected every 4 years. The last congressional elections were held on 17 November 2013, concurrently with the presidential election. The current Senate has a 21–15 split in favor of the governing coalition and 2 independents. The current lower house, the Chamber of Deputies, contains 67 members of the governing center-left coalition, 48 from the center-right opposition and 5 from small parties or independents. The Congress is located in the port city of Valparaíso, about 140 kilometres (87 miles) west of the capital, Santiago.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Congresschile.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Congresschile.jpg/220px-Congresschile.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Congresschile.jpg/330px-Congresschile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/80/Congresschile.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Congresschile.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Chile" title="National Congress of Chile">National Congress</a> building in <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">Valparaíso</a></div></div></div>
<p>Chile's congressional elections are governed by a <a href="/wiki/Binomial_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Binomial System">binomial system</a> that, for the most part, rewards the two largest representations equally, often regardless of their relative popular support. Parties are thus forced to form wide coalitions and, historically, the two largest coalitions (Concertación and Alianza) split most of the seats. Only if the leading coalition ticket out-polls the second place coalition by a margin of more than 2-to-1 does the winning coalition gain both seats, which tends to lock the legislature in a roughly 50–50 split.
</p><p>Chile's judiciary is independent and includes a court of appeal, a system of military courts, a constitutional tribunal, and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Chile" title="Supreme Court of Chile">Supreme Court of Chile</a>. In June 2005, Chile completed a nationwide overhaul of its criminal justice system.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The reform has replaced inquisitorial proceedings with an adversarial system more similar to that of the United States.
</p><p>In the 2001 congressional elections, the conservative <a href="/wiki/Independent_Democratic_Union" title="Independent Democratic Union">Independent Democratic Union</a> (UDI) surpassed the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Party_of_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Party of Chile">Christian Democrats</a> for the first time to become the largest party in the lower house. In the <a href="/wiki/2005_Chilean_parliamentary_election" title="2005 Chilean parliamentary election">2005 parliamentary election</a>, both leading parties, the Christian Democrats and the UDI lost representation in favor of their respective allies <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Chile" title="Socialist Party of Chile">Socialist Party</a> (which became the biggest party in the Concertación block) and <a href="/wiki/National_Renewal_(Chile)" title="National Renewal (Chile)">National Renewal</a> in the right-wing alliance. In the 2009 legislative elections in Chile, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Chile" title="Communist Party of Chile">Communist Party</a> won 3 out of 120 seats in the Chamber of Deputies for the first time in 30 years (the Communist Party was not allowed to exist as such during the dictatorship).
</p><p>Chileans voted in the first round of presidential elections on 17 November 2013. None of the nine presidential candidates got more than 50 percent of the vote. As a result, the top two candidates, center-left <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Mayor%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Nueva Mayoría">Nueva Mayoría</a> coalition's <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet" title="Michelle Bachelet">Michelle Bachelet</a> and center-right <a href="/wiki/Alianza_(Chile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Alianza (Chile)">Alianza</a> coalition's <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Matthei" title="Evelyn Matthei">Evelyn Matthei</a>, competed in a run-off election on 15 December 2013, which Bachelet won. This was Chile's sixth presidential election since the end of the Pinochet era. All six have been judged free and fair. The president is constitutionally barred from serving consecutive terms.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Chile" title="Foreign relations of Chile">Foreign relations of Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Foreign_relations_of_Chile.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Foreign_relations_of_Chile.svg/340px-Foreign_relations_of_Chile.svg.png" decoding="async" width="340" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Foreign_relations_of_Chile.svg/510px-Foreign_relations_of_Chile.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Foreign_relations_of_Chile.svg/680px-Foreign_relations_of_Chile.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Foreign_relations_of_Chile.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>State of Chile's international relations in the world: <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #006680; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Chile</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Country with diplomatic relations and Chilean embassy in the country.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00AA88; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Country with diplomatic relations and an embassy in Chile, but no Chilean embassy.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8DD35F; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Country with diplomatic relations but without ambassadors.</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #cccccc; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Country with no diplomatic relations currently.</div></div></div></div>
<p>Since the early decades after independence, Chile has always had an active involvement in foreign affairs. In 1837 the country aggressively challenged the dominance of Peru's port of <a href="/wiki/Callao" title="Callao">Callao</a> for preeminence in the Pacific trade routes, defeating the short-lived alliance between Peru and Bolivia, the <a href="/wiki/Peru-Bolivian_Confederation" class="mw-redirect" title="Peru-Bolivian Confederation">Peru-Bolivian Confederation</a> (1836–39) in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Confederation" title="War of the Confederation">War of the Confederation</a>. The war dissolved the confederation while distributing power in the Pacific. A second international war, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> (1879–83), further increased Chile's regional role, while adding considerably to its territory.<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 19th century, Chile's commercial ties were primarily with Britain, a nation that had a major influence on the formation of the Chilean navy. The French influenced Chile's legal and educational systems and had a decisive impact on Chile, through the architecture of the capital in the boom years at the turn of the 20th century. German influence came from the organization and training of the army by <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 June 1945, Chile participated as a founding member of the United Nations being among 50 countries that signed the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Charter">United Nations Charter</a> in San Francisco, California.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> With the military coup of 1973, Chile became isolated politically as a result of widespread human rights abuses.<sup id="cite_ref-hudson_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since its return to democracy in 1990, Chile has been an active participant in the international political arena. Chile completed a 2-year non-permanent position on the UN Security Council in January 2005. Jose Miguel Insulza, a Chilean national, was elected Secretary General of the Organization of American States in May 2005 and confirmed in his position, being re-elected in 2009. Chile is currently serving on the International Atomic Energy Agency (IAEA) Board of Governors, and the 2007–2008 chair of the board is Chile's ambassador to the IAEA, Milenko E. Skoknic. The country is an active member of the UN family of agencies and participates in UN peacekeeping activities. It was <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council#Members" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">re-elected</a> as a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">UN Human Rights Council</a> in 2011 for a three-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> It was also <a href="/wiki/2013_United_Nations_Security_Council_election" title="2013 United Nations Security Council election">elected</a> to one of five non-permanent seats on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Chile hosted the Defense Ministerial of the Americas in 2002 and the APEC summit and related meetings in 2004. It also hosted the Community of Democracies ministerial in April 2005 and the Ibero-American Summit in November 2007. An associate member of Mercosur and a full member of APEC, Chile has been a major player in international economic issues and hemispheric free trade.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_disputes_with_Peru">Border disputes with Peru</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Borders_Chile_1879_and_2006_SP.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Borders_Chile_1879_and_2006_SP.png/170px-Borders_Chile_1879_and_2006_SP.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Borders_Chile_1879_and_2006_SP.png/255px-Borders_Chile_1879_and_2006_SP.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Borders_Chile_1879_and_2006_SP.png/340px-Borders_Chile_1879_and_2006_SP.png 2x" data-file-width="363" data-file-height="526" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Borders_Chile_1879_and_2006_SP.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chile's territorial gains after the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> in 1879–83</div></div></div>
<p>There have been long arguments between Chileans and Peruvians since the 1800s because they both claim boundary coastal lines. Peruvians claim the Northern part of Chile, which is now South West of Peru. This also known as the "triangulation" which was made to fix the boundary problem between Chile and Peru. The decisions were accomplished on January 27, 1839 by the International Court of Justice <sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> This became the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> which was in the years 1879-1883.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> This  was caused by the mineral resources Chile had making Peruvians believe it belong to them as well. Chile had to control Sea Shipping to Peru and send out an army to invade Peru on October 8, 1879. The attempt was also made to The United States but failed badly on October 1880. There was a resistance between Peruvians and Chileans for a few years because they couldn't agree. The United States offered help with a treaty for both Peru and Chile, better known as the Treaty of Ancón. This was later signed by both of them on October 20, 1883 to keep peace between them. In 2008, Peru took Chile to court over their maritime disputes. Then later in 2014, the International Court of Justice's ruling resulted in Chile losing 80 miles from Northwestern ocean zone.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> This ruling severely impacted fishers in the country making Chile lose a valuable trade in Northwest Chile.
</p><p>The Chilean Government has diplomatic relations with most countries. It settled all its territorial disputes with Argentina during the 1990s except for part of the border at <a href="/wiki/Southern_Patagonian_Ice_Field" title="Southern Patagonian Ice Field">Southern Patagonian Ice Field</a>. Chile and Bolivia severed diplomatic ties in 1978 over Bolivia's desire to regain sovereign access to the Pacific Ocean after its lost to Chile in 1879–83 War of the Pacific. The two countries maintain consular relations and are represented at the Consul General level.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Chile" title="Administrative divisions of Chile">Administrative divisions of Chile</a></div>
<p>In 1978 Chile was administratively divided into <a href="/wiki/Regions" class="mw-redirect" title="Regions">regions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-dl2339_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dl2339-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and in 1979 subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">provinces</a> and these into communes.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In total the country has <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Chile" title="Regions of Chile">16 regions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-l20174_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-l20174-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-l20175_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-l20175-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Chile" title="Provinces of Chile">56 provinces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Chile" title="Communes of Chile">348 communes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each region is designated by a name and a <a href="/wiki/Roman_numeral" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman numeral">Roman numeral</a> assigned from north to south, except for the <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Metropolitan_Region" title="Santiago Metropolitan Region">Santiago Metropolitan Region</a>, which does not have a number. The creation of two new regions in 2007, Arica and Parinacota (XV) and Los Ríos (XIV), and a third region in 2018, Ñuble (XVI) made this numbering lose its original order meaning.
</p>
<div role="img" class="noresize" style="width: 300px; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_Regiones_de_Chile.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mapa_Regiones_de_Chile.svg/300px-Mapa_Regiones_de_Chile.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="667" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mapa_Regiones_de_Chile.svg/450px-Mapa_Regiones_de_Chile.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mapa_Regiones_de_Chile.svg/600px-Mapa_Regiones_de_Chile.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="288" data-file-height="640" /></a>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:106px; top:352px"><div style="font-size:80%"><a href="/wiki/Araucan%C3%ADa_Region" title="Araucanía Region">Araucanía Region</a></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_symbols">National symbols</span></h3>
<p>The national flower is the <a href="/wiki/Copihue" class="mw-redirect" title="Copihue">copihue</a> (<i>Lapageria rosea</i>, Chilean <a href="/wiki/Campanula" title="Campanula">bellflower</a>), which grows in the woods of southern Chile.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Chile" title="Coat of arms of Chile">coat of arms</a> depicts the two national animals: the <a href="/wiki/Condor" title="Condor">condor</a> (<i>Vultur gryphus</i>, a very large bird that lives in the mountains) and the <a href="/wiki/Hippocamelus" title="Hippocamelus">huemul</a> (<i>Hippocamelus bisulcus,</i> an endangered white tail deer). It also has the legend <i>Por la razón o la fuerza</i> (<i>By reason or by force</i>).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Chile" title="Flag of Chile">flag of Chile</a> consists of two equal horizontal bands of white (top) and red; there is a blue square the same height as the white band at the hoist-side end of the white band; the square bears a white five-pointed star in the center representing a guide to progress and honor; blue symbolizes the sky, white is for the snow-covered Andes, and red stands for the blood spilled to achieve independence. The flag of Chile is similar to the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Texas" title="Flag of Texas">Flag of Texas</a>, although the Chilean flag is 21 years older. However, like the Texan flag, the flag of Chile is modeled after the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States" title="Flag of the United States">Flag of the United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
