href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">F-16 Fighting Falcon</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Air_Force" title="Chilean Air Force">Chilean Air Force</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The Armed Forces of Chile are subject to civilian control exercised by the president through the Minister of Defense. The president has the authority to remove the commanders-in-chief of the armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The commander in chief of the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Army" title="Chilean Army">Chilean Army</a> is <a href="/wiki/General_officer#The_specific_rank_of_general" title="General officer">General</a> Humberto Oviedo Arriagada.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The Chilean Army is 45,000 strong and is organized with an Army headquarters in Santiago, six divisions throughout its territory, an Air Brigade in <a href="/wiki/Rancagua" title="Rancagua">Rancagua</a>, and a Special Forces Command in <a href="/wiki/Colina,_Chile" title="Colina, Chile">Colina</a>. The Chilean Army is one of the most professional and technologically advanced armies in Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Admiral Julio Leiva Molina directs around 25,000-person <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Navy" title="Chilean Navy">Chilean Navy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> including 2,500 Marines. Of the fleet of 29 surface vessels, only eight are operational major combatants (frigates). Those ships are based in <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">Valparaíso</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The Navy operates its own aircraft for transport and patrol; there are no Navy fighter or bomber aircraft. The Navy also operates four submarines based in <a href="/wiki/Talcahuano" title="Talcahuano">Talcahuano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Air Force General (four star) Jorge Rojas Ávila heads the 12,500 strong <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Air_Force" title="Chilean Air Force">Chilean Air Force</a>. Air assets are distributed among five air brigades headquartered in Iquique, Antofagasta, Santiago, Puerto Montt, and Punta Arenas. The Air Force also operates <a href="/wiki/Base_Presidente_Eduardo_Frei_Montalva" title="Base Presidente Eduardo Frei Montalva">an airbase</a> on <a href="/wiki/King_George_Island_(South_Shetland_Islands)" title="King George Island (South Shetland Islands)">King George Island</a>, Antarctica. The Air Force took delivery of the final two of ten F-16s, all purchased from the U.S., in March 2007 after several decades of U.S. debate and previous refusal to sell. Chile also took delivery in 2007 of a number of reconditioned Block 15 F-16s from the Netherlands, bringing to 18 the total of F-16s purchased from the Dutch.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the military coup in September 1973 the <a href="/wiki/Carabineros_de_Chile" title="Carabineros de Chile">Chilean national police</a> (Carabineros) were incorporated into the Defense Ministry. With the return of democratic government, the police were placed under the operational control of the Interior Ministry but remained under the nominal control of the Defense Ministry. Gen. Gustavo González Jure is the head of the national police force of 40,964<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> men and women who are responsible for law enforcement, traffic management, narcotics suppression, border control, and counter-terrorism throughout Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, Chile signed the UN treaty on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Geography.2C_climate.2C_and_environment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography,_climate,_and_environment">Geography, climate, and environment</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Chile" title="Geography of Chile">Geography of Chile</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Natural_regions_of_Chile" title="Natural regions of Chile">Natural regions of Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Chile" title="Environmental issues in Chile">Environmental issues in Chile</a></div>
<div class="noresize thumb tleft" style=";">
<div class="thumbinner" style="overflow:hidden;width:202px;">
<div class="thumbimage" style="overflow:hidden; position:relative; background-color:white;">
<div style=";left:0px; top:0px; width:200px; position:absolute;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg" class="image" title="Natural regions of Chile."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg/200px-Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="449" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg/300px-Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg/400px-Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1183" data-file-height="2658" /></a></div>
<div style="text-align:left; background-color:transparent; line-height:110%;">
<div id="annotation_86x50" style="position:absolute; left:86px; top:50px; line-height:110%"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><b><a href="/wiki/Norte_Grande" title="Norte Grande">Great-Far North</a></b></span></div>
 <div id="annotation_65x125" style="position:absolute; left:65px; top:125px; line-height:110%"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><b><a href="/wiki/Norte_Chico,_Chile" title="Norte Chico, Chile">Northern Zone</a></b></span></div>
 <div id="annotation_45x190" style="position:absolute; left:45px; top:190px; line-height:110%"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><b><a href="/wiki/Central_Chile" title="Central Chile">Central Zone</a></b></span></div>
 <div id="annotation_45x250" style="position:absolute; left:45px; top:250px; line-height:110%"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><b><a href="/wiki/Zona_Sur" title="Zona Sur">Southern Zone</a></b></span></div>
 <div id="annotation_15x360" style="position:absolute; left:15px; top:360px; line-height:110%"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><b><a href="/wiki/Austral_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Austral Zone">Austral Zone</a></b></span></div>
</div>
<div style="visibility:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg/200px-Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="449" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg/300px-Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg/400px-Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1183" data-file-height="2658" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Natural_Regions_of_Chile.svg" title="File:Natural Regions of Chile.svg"> </a></div>Natural regions of Chile.</div>
</div></div>
<p>A long and narrow coastal <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a> country on the west side of the <a href="/wiki/Andes_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Andes Mountains">Andes Mountains</a>, Chile stretches over 4,300&#160;km (2,670&#160;mi) north to south, but only 350&#160;km (217&#160;mi) at its widest point east to west.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> This encompasses a remarkable variety of climates and landscapes. It contains 756,950 square kilometres (292,260&#160;sq&#160;mi) of land area. It is situated within the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ring_of_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Ring of Fire">Pacific Ring of Fire</a>. Excluding its Pacific islands and Antarctic claim, Chile lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_south" title="17th parallel south">17°</a> and <a href="/wiki/56th_parallel_south" title="56th parallel south">56°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/66th_meridian_west" title="66th meridian west">66°</a> and <a href="/wiki/75th_meridian_west" title="75th meridian west">75°W</a>.
</p><p>Chile is among the longest north-south countries in the world. If one considers only mainland territory, Chile is unique within this group in its narrowness from east to west, with the other long north-south countries (including <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, and the United States, among others) all being wider from east to west by a factor of more than 10. Chile also claims 1,250,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (480,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> as part of its territory (<a href="/wiki/Chilean_Antarctic_Territory" title="Chilean Antarctic Territory">Chilean Antarctic Territory</a>). However, this latter claim is suspended under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Antarctic Treaty">Antarctic Treaty</a>, of which Chile is a signatory.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> It is the world's southernmost country that is geographically on the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile controls <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sala_y_G%C3%B3mez" class="mw-redirect" title="Sala y Gómez">Sala y Gómez</a> Island, the easternmost islands of Polynesia, which it incorporated to its territory in 1888, and <a href="/wiki/Robinson_Crusoe_Island" title="Robinson Crusoe Island">Robinson Crusoe Island</a>, more than 600&#160;km (370&#160;mi) from the mainland, in the <a href="/wiki/Juan_Fern%C3%A1ndez_Islands" title="Juan Fernández Islands">Juan Fernández Islands</a>. Also controlled but only temporarily inhabited (by some local fishermen) are the small islands of San Ambrosio and San Felix. These islands are notable because they extend Chile's claim to territorial waters out from its coast into the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The northern <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a> contains great mineral wealth, primarily <a href="/wiki/Copper#Production" title="Copper">copper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caliche_(mineral)#Chilean_caliche" class="mw-redirect" title="Caliche (mineral)">nitrates</a>. The relatively small Central Valley, which includes Santiago, dominates the country in terms of population and agricultural resources. This area is also the historical center from which Chile expanded in the late 19th century, when it integrated the northern and southern regions. Southern Chile is rich in forests, grazing lands, and features a string of volcanoes and lakes. The southern coast is a labyrinth of fjords, inlets, canals, twisting peninsulas, and islands. The Andes Mountains are located on the eastern border.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile_K%C3%B6ppen.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Chile_K%C3%B6ppen.png/200px-Chile_K%C3%B6ppen.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="339" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Chile_K%C3%B6ppen.png/300px-Chile_K%C3%B6ppen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Chile_K%C3%B6ppen.png/400px-Chile_K%C3%B6ppen.png 2x" data-file-width="5100" data-file-height="8638" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile_K%C3%B6ppen.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chile map of Köppen climate classification.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Chile" title="Climate of Chile">Climate of Chile</a></div>
<p>The diverse <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Chile" title="Climate of Chile">climate of Chile</a> ranges from the world's driest desert in the north—the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a>—through a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> in the center, <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a> in Easter Island, to an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Alpine_tundra" title="Alpine tundra">alpine tundra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glaciers" class="mw-redirect" title="Glaciers">glaciers</a> in the east and south.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Chile_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Chile-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen system</a>, Chile within its borders hosts at least ten major climatic subtypes. There are four seasons in most of the country: summer (December to February), autumn (March to May), winter (June to August), and spring (September to November).
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Chile" title="Wildlife of Chile">Wildlife of Chile</a></div>
<p>The flora and fauna of Chile are characterized by a high degree of endemism, due to its particular geography. In continental Chile, the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a> in the north and the <a href="/wiki/Andes_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Andes Mountains">Andes mountains</a> to the east are barriers that have led to the isolation of flora and fauna. Add to that the enormous length of Chile (over 4,300&#160;km (2,672&#160;mi)) and this results in a wide range of climates and environments that can be divided into three general zones: the desert provinces of the north, central Chile, and the humid regions of the south.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Araucaria_araucana_-_Parque_Nacional_Conguill%C3%ADo_por_lautaroj_-_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Araucaria_araucana_-_Parque_Nacional_Conguill%C3%ADo_por_lautaroj_-_001.jpg/220px-Araucaria_araucana_-_Parque_Nacional_Conguill%C3%ADo_por_lautaroj_-_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Araucaria_araucana_-_Parque_Nacional_Conguill%C3%ADo_por_lautaroj_-_001.jpg/330px-Araucaria_araucana_-_Parque_Nacional_Conguill%C3%ADo_por_lautaroj_-_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Araucaria_araucana_-_Parque_Nacional_Conguill%C3%ADo_por_lautaroj_-_001.jpg/440px-Araucaria_araucana_-_Parque_Nacional_Conguill%C3%ADo_por_lautaroj_-_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Araucaria_araucana_-_Parque_Nacional_Conguill%C3%ADo_por_lautaroj_-_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Araucaria araucana</i> trees in Conguillío National Park.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zorrito_Chile.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Zorrito_Chile.JPG/220px-Zorrito_Chile.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Zorrito_Chile.JPG/330px-Zorrito_Chile.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Zorrito_Chile.JPG/440px-Zorrito_Chile.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="576" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zorrito_Chile.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chilla fox, common in the region.</div></div></div>
<p>The native flora of Chile consists of relatively fewer species compared to the flora of other South American countries. 
The northernmost coastal and central region is largely barren of vegetation, approaching the most absolute desert in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Icarito_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Icarito-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
On the slopes of the Andes, in addition to the scattered tola desert brush, grasses are found. The central valley is characterized by several species of cacti, the hardy <a href="/wiki/Acacia_caven" class="mw-redirect" title="Acacia caven">espinos</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Araucaria_araucana" title="Araucaria araucana">Chilean pine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nothofagus" title="Nothofagus">southern beeches</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Copihue" class="mw-redirect" title="Copihue">copihue</a>, a red bell-shaped flower that is Chile's national flower.<sup id="cite_ref-Icarito_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Icarito-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In southern Chile, south of the Biobío River, heavy precipitation has produced dense forests of laurels, magnolias, and various species of conifers and beeches, which become smaller and more stunted to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-Bio&amp;Con_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bio&amp;Con-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
The cold temperatures and winds of the extreme south preclude heavy forestation. Grassland is found in Atlantic Chile (in Patagonia). Much of the Chilean flora is distinct from that of neighboring Argentina, indicating that the Andean barrier existed during its formation.<sup id="cite_ref-Bio&amp;Con_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bio&amp;Con-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Colca-condor-c07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Colca-condor-c07.jpg/220px-Colca-condor-c07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Colca-condor-c07.jpg/330px-Colca-condor-c07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Colca-condor-c07.jpg/440px-Colca-condor-c07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2359" data-file-height="1593" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colca-condor-c07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Andean_condor" title="Andean condor">Andean condor</a> (<i>Vultur gryphus</i>), the national bird of Chile.</div></div></div>
<p>Some of Chile's flora has an Antarctic origin due to <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">land bridges</a> which formed during the Cretaceous ice ages, allowing plants to migrate from Antarctica to South America.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Just over 3,000 species of fungi are recorded in Chile,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> but this number is far from complete. The true total number of fungal species occurring in Chile is likely to be far higher, given the generally accepted estimate that only about 7 percent of all fungi worldwide have so far been discovered.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Although the amount of available information is still very small, a first effort has been made to estimate the number of fungal species endemic to Chile, and 1995 species have been tentatively identified as possible endemics of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile's geographical isolation has restricted the immigration of faunal life, so that only a few of the many distinctive South American animals are found. Among the larger mammals are the <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">puma</a> or cougar, the llama-like <a href="/wiki/Guanaco" title="Guanaco">guanaco</a> and the fox-like <a href="/wiki/South_American_gray_fox" title="South American gray fox">chilla</a>. In the forest region, several types of marsupials and a small deer known as the <a href="/wiki/Pud%C3%BA" title="Pudú">pudu</a> are found.<sup id="cite_ref-Icarito_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Icarito-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are many species of small birds, but most of the larger common Latin American types are absent. Few freshwater fish are native, but North American trout have been successfully introduced into the Andean lakes.<sup id="cite_ref-Icarito_93-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Icarito-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Owing to the vicinity of the Humboldt Current, ocean waters abound with fish and other forms of marine life, which in turn support a rich variety of waterfowl, including several penguins. Whales are abundant, and some six species of seals are found in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Icarito_93-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Icarito-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile_topo_en.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Chile_topo_en.jpg/170px-Chile_topo_en.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="382" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Chile_topo_en.jpg/255px-Chile_topo_en.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Chile_topo_en.jpg/340px-Chile_topo_en.jpg 2x" data-file-width="950" data-file-height="2132" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile_topo_en.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of Chile. To view maps based on <a href="/wiki/SRTM" class="mw-redirect" title="SRTM">SRTM</a> topographic relief of the country, see <a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_Chile/Clickable_map" class="extiw" title="commons:Atlas of Chile/Clickable map">here</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Majestic_Ojos_del_Salado_volcano_(4320230217).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Majestic_Ojos_del_Salado_volcano_%284320230217%29.jpg/220px-Majestic_Ojos_del_Salado_volcano_%284320230217%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Majestic_Ojos_del_Salado_volcano_%284320230217%29.jpg/330px-Majestic_Ojos_del_Salado_volcano_%284320230217%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Majestic_Ojos_del_Salado_volcano_%284320230217%29.jpg/440px-Majestic_Ojos_del_Salado_volcano_%284320230217%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Majestic_Ojos_del_Salado_volcano_(4320230217).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Ojos_del_Salado" title="Ojos del Salado">Ojos del Salado</a> from the Chilean side.</div></div></div>
<p>Chile is located along a highly <a href="/wiki/Seismic" class="mw-redirect" title="Seismic">seismic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> zone, part of the Pacific Ring of Fire, due to the subduction of the Nazca and Antarctic plates in the <a href="/wiki/South_American_plate" class="mw-redirect" title="South American plate">South American plate</a>.
</p><p>Late <a href="/wiki/Paleozoic" title="Paleozoic">Paleozoic</a>, 251 million years ago, Chile belonged to the continental block called Gondwana. It was just a depression accumulated marine sediments began to rise at the end of the Mesozoic, 66 million years ago, due to the collision between the Nazca and South American plates, resulting in the Andes. The territory would be shaped by millions of years due to the folding of the rocks, forming the current relief.
</p><p>The Chilean relief consists of the central depression, which crosses the country longitudinally, flanked by two mountain ranges that make up about 80% of the territory: the Andes mountains to the east-natural border with <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Region" title="Atacama Region">region of Atacama</a> and the Coastal Range west-minor height from the Andes. Chile's highest peak is the <a href="/wiki/Nevado_Ojos_del_Salado" class="mw-redirect" title="Nevado Ojos del Salado">Nevado Ojos del Salado</a>, at 6891.3 m, which is also the highest volcano in the world. The highest point of the Coastal Range is Vicuña Mackenna, at 3114 meters, located in the Sierra Vicuña Mackenna, the south of <a href="/wiki/Antofagasta_Region" title="Antofagasta Region">Antofagasta</a>. Among the coastal mountains and the Pacific is a series of coastal plains, of variable length, which allow the settlement of coastal towns and big ports. Some areas of the plains territories encompass territory east of the Andes, and the Patagonian steppes and Magellan, or are high plateaus surrounded by high mountain ranges, such as the Altiplano or Puna de Atacama.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Far_North,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Far North, Chile">Far North</a> is the area between the northern boundary of the country and the <a href="/wiki/Parallel_(geometry)" title="Parallel (geometry)">parallel</a> 26° S, covering the first three regions. It is characterized by the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Atacama desert">Atacama desert</a>, the most arid in the world. The desert is fragmented by streams that originate in the area known as the <a href="/wiki/Pampa_del_Tamarugal" title="Pampa del Tamarugal">pampas Tamarugal</a>. The Andes, split in two and whose eastern arm runs <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, has a high altitude and volcanic activity, which has allowed the formation of the Andean altiplano and salt structures as the <a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Atacama" title="Salar de Atacama">Salar de Atacama</a>, due to the gradual accumulation of sediments over time.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Volcano_Osorno_and_Petrohu%C3%A9_waterfalls.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Volcano_Osorno_and_Petrohu%C3%A9_waterfalls.JPG/220px-Volcano_Osorno_and_Petrohu%C3%A9_waterfalls.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Volcano_Osorno_and_Petrohu%C3%A9_waterfalls.JPG/330px-Volcano_Osorno_and_Petrohu%C3%A9_waterfalls.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Volcano_Osorno_and_Petrohu%C3%A9_waterfalls.JPG/440px-Volcano_Osorno_and_Petrohu%C3%A9_waterfalls.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Volcano_Osorno_and_Petrohu%C3%A9_waterfalls.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Osorno_(volcano)" title="Osorno (volcano)">Osorno Volcano</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Petrohu%C3%A9_River" title="Petrohué River">Petrohué River</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glaciar_y_laguna_Nef,_afluente_Baker,.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Glaciar_y_laguna_Nef%2C_afluente_Baker%2C.JPG/220px-Glaciar_y_laguna_Nef%2C_afluente_Baker%2C.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Glaciar_y_laguna_Nef%2C_afluente_Baker%2C.JPG/330px-Glaciar_y_laguna_Nef%2C_afluente_Baker%2C.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Glaciar_y_laguna_Nef%2C_afluente_Baker%2C.JPG/440px-Glaciar_y_laguna_Nef%2C_afluente_Baker%2C.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glaciar_y_laguna_Nef,_afluente_Baker,.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nef_Glacier" title="Nef Glacier">Nef Glacier</a> and the Plomo Lake</div></div></div>
<p>To the south is the <a href="/wiki/Norte_Chico,_Chile" title="Norte Chico, Chile">Norte Chico</a>, extending to the <a href="/wiki/Aconcagua_River" title="Aconcagua River">Aconcagua river</a>. Los Andes begin to decrease its altitude to the south and closer to the coast, reaching 90&#160;km away at the height of <a href="/wiki/Illapel" title="Illapel">Illapel</a>, the narrowest part of the Chilean territory. The two mountain ranges intersect, virtually eliminating the intermediate depression. The existence of rivers flowing through the territory allows the formation of <a href="/wiki/Transverse_Valleys" title="Transverse Valleys">transverse valleys</a>, where agriculture has developed strongly in recent times, while the <a href="/wiki/Coastal_plains" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastal plains">coastal plains</a> begin to expand.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Zona_Central,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Zona Central, Chile">Central</a> area is the most populated region of the country. The coastal plains are wide and allow the establishment of cities and ports along the Pacific. The Andes maintains altitudes above 6000m but descend slowly starts approaching the 4000 meters on average. The intermediate depression reappears becoming a fertile valley that allows agricultural development and human settlement, due to sediment accumulation. To the south, the Cordillera de la Costa reappears in the <a href="/wiki/Nahuelbuta_Range" class="mw-redirect" title="Nahuelbuta Range">range of Nahuelbuta</a> while glacial sediments originate a series of lakes in the area of <a href="/wiki/La_Frontera,_Chile" title="La Frontera, Chile">La Frontera</a>.
</p><p>Patagonia extends from within Reloncavi, at the height of parallel 41°S, to the south. During the <a href="/wiki/Llanquihue_glaciation" title="Llanquihue glaciation">last glaciation</a>, this area was covered by ice that strongly eroded Chilean relief structures. As a result, the intermediate depression sinks in the sea, while the coastal mountains rise to a series of archipelagos, such as <a href="/wiki/Chilo%C3%A9_Island" title="Chiloé Island">Chiloé</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chonos_Archipelago" title="Chonos Archipelago">Chonos</a>, disappearing in Taitao peninsula, in the parallel 47°S. The Andes mountain range loses height and erosion caused by the action of glaciers has caused <a href="/wiki/Fjords" class="mw-redirect" title="Fjords">fjords</a>.
</p><p>East of the Andes, on the continent, or north of it, on the <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego_(main_island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tierra del Fuego (main island)">island of Tierra del Fuego</a> are located relatively flat plains, which in the Strait of Magellan cover large areas.
</p><p>The Andes, as he had done previously Cordillera de la Costa, begins to break in the ocean causing a myriad of islands and islets and disappear into it, sinking and reappearing in the Southern Antilles arc and then the Antarctic Peninsula, where it is called Antartandes, in the Chilean Antarctic Territory, lying between the meridians 53°W and 90°W.
</p><p>In the middle of the Pacific, the country has sovereignty over several islands of volcanic origin, collectively known as Insular Chile. Of these, we highlight the archipelago of Juan Fernandez and Easter Island, which is located in the fracture zone between the Nazca plate and the Pacific plate known as East Pacific Rise.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">Hydrography</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lago_General_Carrera_-_Camino_a_Capilla_de_M%C3%A1rmol.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Lago_General_Carrera_-_Camino_a_Capilla_de_M%C3%A1rmol.JPG/220px-Lago_General_Carrera_-_Camino_a_Capilla_de_M%C3%A1rmol.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Lago_General_Carrera_-_Camino_a_Capilla_de_M%C3%A1rmol.JPG/330px-Lago_General_Carrera_-_Camino_a_Capilla_de_M%C3%A1rmol.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Lago_General_Carrera_-_Camino_a_Capilla_de_M%C3%A1rmol.JPG/440px-Lago_General_Carrera_-_Camino_a_Capilla_de_M%C3%A1rmol.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lago_General_Carrera_-_Camino_a_Capilla_de_M%C3%A1rmol.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/General_Carrera_Lake" title="General Carrera Lake">General Carrera lake</a>, the largest in the country.</div></div></div>
<p>Due to the characteristics of the territory, Chile is crossed by numerous rivers generally short in length and with low torrential flow. They commonly extend from the <a href="/wiki/Andes_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Andes Mountains">Andes</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, flowing in an East to West.
</p><p>Because of the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Atacama desert">Atacama desert</a>, in the Norte Grande there are only short <a href="/wiki/Endorheic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endorheic">endorheic</a> character streams, except for the <a href="/wiki/Loa_River" title="Loa River">Loa River</a>, the longest in the country 440&#160;km.<sup id="cite_ref-hydr_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hydr-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In the high valleys, wetland areas generate <a href="/wiki/Chungar%C3%A1_Lake" title="Chungará Lake">Chungará Lake</a>, located at 4500 meters above sea level. It and the <a href="/wiki/Lauca_River" title="Lauca River">Lauca River</a> are shared with <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Lluta_River" title="Lluta River">Lluta River</a>.
</p><p>In the center-north of the country, the number of rivers that form valleys of agricultural importance increases. Noteworthy are the Elqui with 75&#160;km<sup id="cite_ref-hydr_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hydr-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> long, 142&#160;km Aconcagua, Maipo with 250&#160;km<sup id="cite_ref-hydr_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hydr-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and its tributary, the Mapocho with 110&#160;km, and Maule with 240&#160;km. Their waters mainly flow from Andean snowmelt in the summer and winter rains. The major lakes in this area are the artificial lake Rapel, the Colbun Maule lagoon and the lagoon of La Laja.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile-demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Chile-demography.png/300px-Chile-demography.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Chile-demography.png/450px-Chile-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Chile-demography.png/600px-Chile-demography.png 2x" data-file-width="1476" data-file-height="939" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile-demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population of Chile from 1820, projected up to 2050</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Chile" title="Demographics of Chile">Demographics of Chile</a></div>
<p>Chile's 2017 census reported a population of 17,574,003. Its rate of population growth has been decreasing since 1990, due to a declining <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> By 2050 the population is expected to reach approximately 20.2 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> About 85 percent of the country's population lives in urban areas, with 40 percent living in <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Greater Santiago</a>. The largest agglomerations according to the 2002 census are Greater Santiago with 5.6 million people, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="Greater Concepción">Greater Concepción</a> with 861,000
and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Greater Valparaíso">Greater Valparaíso</a> with 824,000.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry_and_ethnicity">Ancestry and ethnicity</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Chile" title="Indigenous peoples in Chile">Indigenous peoples in Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Chile" title="Immigration to Chile">Immigration to Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ministro_Osorio_entrega_terreno_a_Comunidad_Mapuche_Lorenzo_Quintrileo_de_Tir%C3%BAa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Ministro_Osorio_entrega_terreno_a_Comunidad_Mapuche_Lorenzo_Quintrileo_de_Tir%C3%BAa.jpg/220px-Ministro_Osorio_entrega_terreno_a_Comunidad_Mapuche_Lorenzo_Quintrileo_de_Tir%C3%BAa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Ministro_Osorio_entrega_terreno_a_Comunidad_Mapuche_Lorenzo_Quintrileo_de_Tir%C3%BAa.jpg/330px-Ministro_Osorio_entrega_terreno_a_Comunidad_Mapuche_Lorenzo_Quintrileo_de_Tir%C3%BAa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Ministro_Osorio_entrega_terreno_a_Comunidad_Mapuche_Lorenzo_Quintrileo_de_Tir%C3%BAa.jpg/440px-Ministro_Osorio_entrega_terreno_a_Comunidad_Mapuche_Lorenzo_Quintrileo_de_Tir%C3%BAa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ministro_Osorio_entrega_terreno_a_Comunidad_Mapuche_Lorenzo_Quintrileo_de_Tir%C3%BAa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mapuche women of <a href="/wiki/Tir%C3%BAa" title="Tirúa">Tirúa</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1951_settler_families.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/1951_settler_families.JPG/220px-1951_settler_families.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/1951_settler_families.JPG/330px-1951_settler_families.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/1951_settler_families.JPG/440px-1951_settler_families.JPG 2x" data-file-width="647" data-file-height="438" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1951_settler_families.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>German immigrants in southern Chile</div></div></div>
<p>The 1907 census reported 101,118 Natives, or 3.1% of the total population. Only those that practiced their native culture or spoke their native language were considered to be Natives, irrespective of their "racial purity".<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2002 a census took place, directly asking the public whether they considered themselves as part of any of the eight Chilean ethnic groups, regardless of whether or not they maintained their culture, traditions and language, and 4.6 percent of the population (692,192 people) fitted that description of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Chile" title="Indigenous peoples in Chile">indigenous peoples in Chile</a>. Of that number, 87.3% declared themselves Mapuche.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Most of the indigenous population shows varying degrees of mixed ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-medwave_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-medwave-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile is one of 22 countries to have signed and ratified the only binding international law concerning indigenous peoples, the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_and_Tribal_Peoples_Convention,_1989" title="Indigenous and Tribal Peoples Convention, 1989">Indigenous and Tribal Peoples Convention, 1989</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> It was adopted in 1989 as the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> (ILO) Convention 169. Chile ratified it in 2008. A Chilean court decision in November 2009 considered to be a landmark ruling on indigenous rights and made use of the convention. The Supreme Court decision on Aymara water rights upheld rulings by both the Pozo Almonte tribunal and the Iquique Court of Appeals, and marks the first judicial application of ILO Convention 169 in Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile was never a particularly attractive destination for migrants, owing to its remoteness and distance from Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Euzko_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euzko-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Europeans preferred to stay in countries closer to their homelands instead of taking the long journey through the Straits of Magellan or crossing the Andes.<sup id="cite_ref-Euzko_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euzko-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> European migration did not result in a significant change in the ethnic composition of Chile, except in the <a href="/wiki/Magallanes_y_la_Ant%C3%A1rtica_Chilena_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Magallanes y la Antártica Chilena Region">region of Magellan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-C1907_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C1907-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Spaniards were the only major European migrant group to Chile,<sup id="cite_ref-Euzko_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euzko-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> and there was never large-scale immigration such as that to Argentina or Uruguay.<sup id="cite_ref-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Between 1851 and 1924, Chile only received 0.5% of European immigration to Latin America, compared to 46% to Argentina, 33% to Brazil, 14% to Cuba, and 4% to Uruguay.<sup id="cite_ref-Euzko_109-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euzko-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> However, it is undeniable that immigrants have played a significant role in Chilean society.<sup id="cite_ref-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other groups of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">Europeans</a> have followed but are found in smaller numbers, like the descendants of <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">Austrians</a><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch people</a>. Currently, these are estimated at about 50,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> After the failed <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_German_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the German states">liberal revolution of 1848</a> in the German states,<sup id="cite_ref-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile_110-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> a noticeable German immigration took place, laying the foundation for the <a href="/wiki/German_Chileans" title="German Chileans">German Chileans</a>. Sponsored by the Chilean government to "unbarbarize" and colonize the southern region,<sup id="cite_ref-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile_110-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoriaContemporaneaDeChile-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> these Germans (notably the Swiss, Silesians, Alsatians and Austrians) settled mainly in <a href="/wiki/German_colonization_of_Valdivia,_Osorno_and_Llanquihue" title="German colonization of Valdivia, Osorno and Llanquihue">Valdivia, Osorno and Llanquihue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Descendants of different <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European ethnic groups</a> often intermarried in Chile. This intermarriage and mixture of cultures and races have helped to shape the present society and culture of the Chilean middle and upper classes.<sup id="cite_ref-deia.com_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deia.com-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due in part to its economic fortunes, Chile has recently become a new magnet for immigrants, mostly from neighboring Venezuela, Peru, Haiti, Colombia, Bolivia and Argentina.<sup id="cite_ref-Censo,_2017_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Censo,_2017-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> According to the 2002 national census, Chile's foreign-born population has increased by 75% since 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> According to an estimate by the Migration and Foreign Residency Department 1,200,000 foreigners were living in Chile in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Censo,_2017_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Censo,_2017-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>  Roughly 500,000 of Chile's population is of full or partial <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian origin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Chile" title="Religion in Chile">Religion in Chile</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catedral_Metropolitana_de_Santiago.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Catedral_Metropolitana_de_Santiago.jpg/200px-Catedral_Metropolitana_de_Santiago.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Catedral_Metropolitana_de_Santiago.jpg/300px-Catedral_Metropolitana_de_Santiago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Catedral_Metropolitana_de_Santiago.jpg/400px-Catedral_Metropolitana_de_Santiago.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1843" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catedral_Metropolitana_de_Santiago.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Cathedral_of_Santiago" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Cathedral of Santiago">Metropolitan Cathedral of Santiago</a></div></div></div>
<p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chile&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 66.6%<sup id="cite_ref-censo.cl_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censo.cl-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> of Chilean population over 15 years of age claimed to adhere to the Roman Catholic church, a decrease from the 70%<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> reported in the 2002 census.  In the same census of 2012, 17% of Chileans reported adherence to an Evangelical church ("Evangelical" in the census referred to all Christian denominations other than the Roman Catholic and <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a>—Greek, Persian, Serbian, Ukrainian, and Armenian—churches, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>:  essentially, those denominations generally still termed "<a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestant</a>" in most English-speaking lands, although <a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">Adventism</a> is often considered an Evangelical denomination as well).  Approximately 90% of Evangelical Christians are <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a>. but <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan_Church" title="Wesleyan Church">Wesleyan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Episcopalian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian">Presbyterian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reformed_churches" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed churches">other Reformed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Methodist_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist church">Methodist churches</a> also are present amongst Chilean Evangelical churches.<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedomreport_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedomreport-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>  Irreligious people, atheists, and agnostics account for around 12% of the population.
</p><p>By 2015, the major religion in Chile remained Christianity (68%), with an estimated 55% of Chileans belonging to the Roman Catholic church, 13% to various Evangelical churches, and just 7% adhering to any other religion.  Agnostics and atheist were estimated at 25% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile has a <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá&#39;í">Bahá'í</a> religious community, and is home to the mother temple of the Bahá'ís for Latin America, which was completed in 2016 and has been described as futuristic and translucent in its architectural style.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Constitution guarantees the right to <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>, and other laws and policies contribute to generally free religious practice.  The law at all levels fully protects this right against abuse by either governmental or private actors.<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedomreport_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedomreport-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Church and state are officially <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">separate</a> in Chile.  A 1999 law on religion prohibits <a href="/wiki/Religious_discrimination" title="Religious discrimination">religious discrimination</a>. 
However, the Roman Catholic church for mostly historical and social reasons enjoys a privileged status and occasionally receives preferential treatment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  Government officials attend Roman Catholic events as well as major Evangelical and Jewish ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedomreport_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedomreport-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_la_ciudad_desde_los_jardines.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vista_de_la_ciudad_desde_los_jardines.png/220px-Vista_de_la_ciudad_desde_los_jardines.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vista_de_la_ciudad_desde_los_jardines.png/330px-Vista_de_la_ciudad_desde_los_jardines.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vista_de_la_ciudad_desde_los_jardines.png/440px-Vista_de_la_ciudad_desde_los_jardines.png 2x" data-file-width="4496" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_la_ciudad_desde_los_jardines.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bahá’í House of Worship for South America</div></div></div>
<p>The Chilean government treats the religious holidays of Christmas, <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Mount_Carmel" title="Our Lady of Mount Carmel">Feast of the Virgin of Carmen</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_Saints_Peter_and_Paul" title="Feast of Saints Peter and Paul">Feast of Saints Peter and Paul</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">Feast of the Assumption</a>, <a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day" title="All Saints&#39; Day">All Saints' Day</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_the_Immaculate_Conception" title="Feast of the Immaculate Conception">Feast of the Immaculate Conception</a> as <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">national holidays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedomreport_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedomreport-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>  Recently, the government declared 31 October, <a href="/wiki/Reformation_Day" title="Reformation Day">Reformation Day</a>, to be an additional national holiday, in honor of the Evangelical churches of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saints</a> of Chile are <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Mount_Carmel" title="Our Lady of Mount Carmel">Our Lady of Mount Carmel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_James_the_Greater" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint James the Greater">Saint James the Greater</a> (<i>Santiago</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>  In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> canonized <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Hurtado" title="Alberto Hurtado">Alberto Hurtado</a>, who became the country's second native Roman Catholic saint after <a href="/wiki/Teresa_de_los_Andes" class="mw-redirect" title="Teresa de los Andes">Teresa de los Andes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Spanish" title="Chilean Spanish">Spanish spoken in Chile</a> is distinctively accented and quite unlike that of neighboring South American countries because final syllables are often dropped, and some consonants have a soft pronunciation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="Which consonants and what kind of soft pronunciation? (April 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Accent varies only very slightly from north to south; more noticeable are the differences in accent based on social class or whether one lives in the city or the country. That the Chilean population was largely formed in a small section at the center of the country and then migrated in modest numbers to the north and south helps explain this relative lack of differentiation, which was maintained by the national reach of radio, and now television, which also helps to diffuse and homogenize colloquial expressions.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are several indigenous languages spoken in Chile: <a href="/wiki/Mapudungun" class="mw-redirect" title="Mapudungun">Mapudungun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Quechua" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilean Quechua">Quechua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui_language" title="Rapa Nui language">Rapa Nui</a>. After the Spanish invasion, Spanish took over as the <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> and the indigenous languages have become minority languages, with some now extinct or close to extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>German is still spoken to some extent in southern Chile,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> either in small country side pockets or as a second language among the communities of larger cities.
</p><p>Through initiatives such as the <a href="/wiki/English_Opens_Doors" title="English Opens Doors">English Opens Doors Program</a>, the government made English mandatory for students in fifth-grade and above in public schools. Most private schools in Chile start teaching English from kindergarten.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Common English words have been absorbed and appropriated into everyday Spanish speech.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_Central_Pontificia_Universidad_Catolica_de_Chile.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Pontificical Catholic University of Chile (PUC)." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Casa_Central_Pontificia_Universidad_Catolica_de_Chile.JPG/200px-Casa_Central_Pontificia_Universidad_Catolica_de_Chile.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Casa_Central_Pontificia_Universidad_Catolica_de_Chile.JPG/300px-Casa_Central_Pontificia_Universidad_Catolica_de_Chile.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Casa_Central_Pontificia_Universidad_Catolica_de_Chile.JPG/400px-Casa_Central_Pontificia_Universidad_Catolica_de_Chile.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Chile" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Chile">Pontifical Catholic University of Chile (PUC)</a>.</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_Central_de_la_Universidad_de_Chile.jpg" class="image"><img alt="University of Chile (UCh)." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Casa_Central_de_la_Universidad_de_Chile.jpg/200px-Casa_Central_de_la_Universidad_de_Chile.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="111" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Casa_Central_de_la_Universidad_de_Chile.jpg/300px-Casa_Central_de_la_Universidad_de_Chile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Casa_Central_de_la_Universidad_de_Chile.jpg/400px-Casa_Central_de_la_Universidad_de_Chile.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2303" data-file-height="1277" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/University_of_Chile" title="University of Chile">University of Chile (UCh).</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Arco_de_Medicina_UdeC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="University of Concepción (UdeC)." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Arco_de_Medicina_UdeC.jpg/200px-Arco_de_Medicina_UdeC.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Arco_de_Medicina_UdeC.jpg/300px-Arco_de_Medicina_UdeC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Arco_de_Medicina_UdeC.jpg/400px-Arco_de_Medicina_UdeC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/University_of_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="University of Concepción">University of Concepción (UdeC).</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Chile" title="Education in Chile">Education in Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Chile" title="List of universities in Chile">List of universities in Chile</a></div>
<p>In Chile, education begins with <a href="/wiki/Preschool" title="Preschool">preschool</a> until the age of 5. <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">Primary school</a> is provided for children between ages 6 and 13. Students then attend <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a> until graduation at age 17.
</p><p>Secondary education is divided into two parts: During the first two years, students receive a general education. Then, they choose a branch: scientific humanistic education, artistic education, or technical and professional education. Secondary school ends two years later on the acquirement of a certificate (licencia de enseñanza media).<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chilean education is segregated by wealth in a three-tiered system — the quality of the schools reflect socioeconomic backgrounds:
</p>
<ul><li>city schools (colegios municipales) that are mostly free and have the worse education results, mostly attended by poor students;</li>
<li>subsidized schools that receive some money from the government which can be supplemented by fees paid by the student's family, which are attended by mid-income students and typically get mid-level results; and</li>
<li>entirely private schools that consistently get the best results. Many private schools charge attendance fees of 0,5 to 1 median household incomes.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Upon successful graduation of secondary school, students may continue into <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>. The higher education schools in Chile consist of <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Traditional_Universities" title="Chilean Traditional Universities">Chilean Traditional Universities</a> and are divided into <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public universities</a> or <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private universities</a>. There are <a href="/wiki/List_of_medical_schools_in_South_America#Chile" title="List of medical schools in South America">medical schools</a> and both the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_de_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad de Chile">Universidad de Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Diego_Portales" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Diego Portales">Universidad Diego Portales</a> offer <a href="/wiki/Legal_education" title="Legal education">law schools</a> in a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Chile" title="Healthcare in Chile">Healthcare in Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fonasa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Fonasa.jpg/170px-Fonasa.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Fonasa.jpg/255px-Fonasa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Fonasa.jpg/340px-Fonasa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="2398" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fonasa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>FONASA is the funding branch of the Ministry of Health.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_(Chile)" title="Ministry of Health (Chile)">Ministry of Health</a> (<i>Minsal</i>) is the cabinet-level administrative office in charge of planning, directing, coordinating, executing, controlling and informing the public health policies formulated by the President of Chile. The <a href="/wiki/Fondo_Nacional_de_Salud" title="Fondo Nacional de Salud">National Health Fund</a> (<i>Fonasa</i>), created in 1979, is the financial entity entrusted to collect, manage and distribute state funds for health in Chile. It is funded by the public. All employees pay 7 percent of their monthly income to the fund.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Fonasa is part of the NHSS and has executive power through the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_(Chile)" title="Ministry of Health (Chile)">Ministry of Health (Chile)</a>. Its headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago, Chile">Santiago</a> and decentralized public service is conducted by various Regional Offices. More than 12 million beneficiaries benefit from Fonasa. Beneficiaries can also opt for more costly private insurance through <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isapre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Isapre (page does not exist)">Isapre</a>. <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Chile" title="List of hospitals in Chile">Hospitals in Chile</a> are mainly located in the <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Metropolitan_Region" title="Santiago Metropolitan Region">Santiago Metropolitan Region</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Chile" title="Economy of Chile">Economy of Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile_and_Latin_America_GDP_Average.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Chile_and_Latin_America_GDP_Average.png/220px-Chile_and_Latin_America_GDP_Average.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Chile_and_Latin_America_GDP_Average.png/330px-Chile_and_Latin_America_GDP_Average.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Chile_and_Latin_America_GDP_Average.png/440px-Chile_and_Latin_America_GDP_Average.png 2x" data-file-width="852" data-file-height="490" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chile_and_Latin_America_GDP_Average.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chilean (blue) and average Latin American (orange) <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> (1980–2017)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gran_Torre_Santiago_(39693576311).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Gran_Torre_Santiago_%2839693576311%29.jpg/220px-Gran_Torre_Santiago_%2839693576311%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Gran_Torre_Santiago_%2839693576311%29.jpg/330px-Gran_Torre_Santiago_%2839693576311%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Gran_Torre_Santiago_%2839693576311%29.jpg/440px-Gran_Torre_Santiago_%2839693576311%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2866" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gran_Torre_Santiago_(39693576311).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The financial district in Santiago de Chile</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolsa_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bolsa_2.JPG/220px-Bolsa_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bolsa_2.JPG/330px-Bolsa_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bolsa_2.JPG/440px-Bolsa_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1369" data-file-height="907" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolsa_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Santiago_Stock_Exchange" title="Santiago Stock Exchange">Santiago Stock Exchange</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chuquicamata-003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Chuquicamata-003.jpg/220px-Chuquicamata-003.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Chuquicamata-003.jpg/330px-Chuquicamata-003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Chuquicamata-003.jpg/440px-Chuquicamata-003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2126" data-file-height="1380" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chuquicamata-003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chuquicamata" title="Chuquicamata">Chuquicamata</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Open-pit_mining" title="Open-pit mining">open pit</a> <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> mine in the world</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Chile" title="Central Bank of Chile">Central Bank of Chile</a> in Santiago serves as the <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> for the country. The Chilean currency is the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_peso" title="Chilean peso">Chilean peso</a> (CLP). Chile is one of South America's most stable and prosperous nations,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Chile_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Chile-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> leading Latin American nations in <a href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Human development (humanity)">human development</a>, competitiveness, income per capita, globalization, economic freedom, and low perception of corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Since July 2013, Chile is considered by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> as a "<a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income economy</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-wb_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:75_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:75-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:76_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:76-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile has the highest degree of <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">economic freedom</a> in South America (ranking 7th worldwide), owing to its independent and efficient judicial system and prudent public finance management.<sup id="cite_ref-iefhf_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iefhf-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In May 2010 Chile became the first South American country to join the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, Chile became the country with the highest nominal GDP per capita in Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Copper mining makes up 20% of Chilean GDP and 60% of exports.<sup id="cite_ref-coppersol_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coppersol-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Escondida" title="Escondida">Escondida</a> is the largest copper mine in the world, producing over 5% of global supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-coppersol_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coppersol-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Overall, Chile produces a third of the world's copper.<sup id="cite_ref-coppersol_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coppersol-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Codelco" title="Codelco">Codelco</a>, the state mining firm, competes with private copper mining companies.<sup id="cite_ref-coppersol_144-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coppersol-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sound economic policies, maintained consistently since the 1980s, have contributed to steady economic growth in Chile and have more than halved poverty rates.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Chile began to experience a moderate economic downturn in 1999. The economy remained sluggish until 2003, when it began to show clear signs of recovery, achieving 4.0% GDP growth.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The Chilean economy finished 2004 with growth of 6 percent. Real GDP growth reached 5.7 percent in 2005 before falling back to 4 percent in 2006. GDP expanded by 5 percent in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Faced with an <a href="/wiki/2008_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 financial crisis">international economic downturn</a> the government announced an economic stimulus plan to spur employment and growth, and despite the global financial crisis, aimed for an expansion of between 2 percent and 3 percent of GDP for 2009. Nonetheless, economic analysts disagreed with government estimates and predicted economic growth at a median of 1.5 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Real GDP growth in 2012 was 5.5%. Growth slowed to 4.1% in the first quarter of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-imfartiv_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfartiv-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The unemployment rate was 6.4% in April 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> There are reported labor shortages in agriculture, mining, and construction.<sup id="cite_ref-imfartiv_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfartiv-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The percentage of Chileans with per capita household incomes below the poverty line—defined as twice the cost of satisfying a person's minimal nutritional needs—fell from 45.1 percent in 1987 to 11.5 percent in 2009, according to government surveys.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Critics in Chile, however, argue that true poverty figures are considerably higher than those officially published.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Using the relative yardstick favoured in many European countries, 27% of Chileans would be poor, according to Juan Carlos Feres of the <a href="/wiki/ECLAC" class="mw-redirect" title="ECLAC">ECLAC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
