</p><p>As of November&#160;2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chile&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, about 11.1 million people (64% of the population) benefit from government welfare programs,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> via the "Social Protection Card", which includes the population living in poverty and those at a risk of falling into poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chile_pension_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Chile pension system">The privatized national pension system</a> (AFP) has encouraged domestic investment and contributed to an estimated total domestic savings rate of approximately 21 percent of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Under the compulsory private pension system, most formal sector employees pay 10 percent of their salaries into privately managed funds.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile has signed <a href="/wiki/Free_trade_agreements" class="mw-redirect" title="Free trade agreements">free trade agreements</a> (FTAs) with a whole network of countries, including an FTA with the United States that was signed in 2003 and implemented in January 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Internal Government of Chile figures show that even when factoring out inflation and the recent high price of copper, bilateral trade between the U.S. and Chile has grown over 60 percent since then.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Chile's total trade with China reached US in 2006, representing nearly 66 percent of the value of its trade relationship with Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Exports to Asia increased from US in 2005 to US in 2006, a 29.9 percent increase.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Year-on-year growth in imports was especially strong from a number of countries: Ecuador (123.9%), Thailand (72.1%), South Korea (52.6%), and China (36.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chile's approach to foreign direct investment is codified in the country's Foreign Investment Law. Registration is reported to be simple and transparent, and foreign investors are guaranteed access to the official <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange market</a> to repatriate their profits and capital.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
The Chilean Government has formed a Council on Innovation and Competition, hoping to bring in additional FDI to new parts of the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor&#39;s">Standard &amp; Poor's</a> gives Chile a <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">credit rating</a> of AA-.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The Government of Chile continues to pay down its foreign debt, with public debt only 3.9 percent of GDP at the end of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies_27-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The Chilean central government is a net creditor with a <a href="/wiki/Net_asset_value" title="Net asset value">net asset position</a> of 7% of GDP at end 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-imfartiv_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfartiv-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Current_account_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Current account deficit">current account deficit</a> was 4% in the first quarter of 2013, financed mostly by foreign direct investment.<sup id="cite_ref-imfartiv_147-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfartiv-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> 14% of central government revenue came directly from copper in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-imfartiv_147-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfartiv-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mineral_resources">Mineral resources</span></h3>
<p>Chile is rich in mineral resources, especially copper and lithium. It is thought that due to the importance of lithium for batteries for electric vehicles and stabilization of electric grids with large proportions of intermittent renewables in the electricity mix, Chile could be strengthened geopolitically. However, this perspective has also been criticised for underestimating the power of economic incentives for expanded production in other parts of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Chile" title="Agriculture in Chile">Agriculture in Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_general_de_Valle_de_Casablanca.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Vista_general_de_Valle_de_Casablanca.jpg/220px-Vista_general_de_Valle_de_Casablanca.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Vista_general_de_Valle_de_Casablanca.jpg/330px-Vista_general_de_Valle_de_Casablanca.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Vista_general_de_Valle_de_Casablanca.jpg/440px-Vista_general_de_Valle_de_Casablanca.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_general_de_Valle_de_Casablanca.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vineyard in the <a href="/wiki/Casablanca_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Casablanca Valley">Casablanca Valley</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> in Chile encompasses a wide range of different activities due to its particular <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geology</a> and human factors. Historically agriculture is one of the bases of Chile's economy. Now agriculture and allied sectors like <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">logging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> account for only 4.9% of the <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> as of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chile&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> and employ 13.6% of the country's labor force. Some major agriculture products of Chile include <a href="/wiki/Grapes" class="mw-redirect" title="Grapes">grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">apples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pear" title="Pear">pears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">onions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corn" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oats" class="mw-redirect" title="Oats">oats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peach" title="Peach">peaches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asparagus" title="Asparagus">asparagus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timber" class="mw-redirect" title="Timber">timber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hemp" title="Hemp">hemp</a>.[1] Due to its geographical isolation and strict customs policies Chile is free from diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Mad_Cow_Disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Mad Cow Disease">Mad Cow Disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drosophilidae" title="Drosophilidae">fruit fly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phylloxera" title="Phylloxera">Phylloxera</a>. This, its location in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>, which has quite different harvesting times from the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a>, and its wide range of agriculture conditions are considered Chile's main comparative advantages. However, Chile's mountainous landscape limits the extent and intensity of agriculture so that arable land corresponds only to 2.62% of the total territory. Chile currently utilizes 14,015 Hectares of agricultural land.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Chile" title="Tourism in Chile">Tourism in Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salar_de_Atacama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Salar_de_Atacama.jpg/220px-Salar_de_Atacama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Salar_de_Atacama.jpg/330px-Salar_de_Atacama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Salar_de_Atacama.jpg/440px-Salar_de_Atacama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salar_de_Atacama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Atacama" title="Salar de Atacama">Salar de Atacama</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Desert" title="Atacama Desert">Atacama Desert</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valle_del_Elqui,_La_Serena-Chile.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Valle_del_Elqui%2C_La_Serena-Chile.JPG/220px-Valle_del_Elqui%2C_La_Serena-Chile.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Valle_del_Elqui%2C_La_Serena-Chile.JPG/330px-Valle_del_Elqui%2C_La_Serena-Chile.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Valle_del_Elqui%2C_La_Serena-Chile.JPG/440px-Valle_del_Elqui%2C_La_Serena-Chile.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2952" data-file-height="1974" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valle_del_Elqui,_La_Serena-Chile.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Elqui_Valley_(wine_region)" title="Elqui Valley (wine region)">Elqui Valley</a>, wine and pisco region</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cerro_Concepcion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Cerro_Concepcion.jpg/220px-Cerro_Concepcion.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Cerro_Concepcion.jpg/330px-Cerro_Concepcion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Cerro_Concepcion.jpg/440px-Cerro_Concepcion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1060" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cerro_Concepcion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">Valparaíso</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Varas_Osorno.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Puerto_Varas_Osorno.jpg/220px-Puerto_Varas_Osorno.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Puerto_Varas_Osorno.jpg/330px-Puerto_Varas_Osorno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Puerto_Varas_Osorno.jpg/440px-Puerto_Varas_Osorno.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="532" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Varas_Osorno.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Varas" title="Puerto Varas">Puerto Varas</a></div></div></div>
<p>Tourism in Chile has experienced sustained growth over the last few decades. In 2005, tourism grew by 13.6 percent, generating more than 4.5 billion dollars of which 1.5 billion was attributed to foreign tourists. According to the National Service of Tourism (Sernatur), 2 million people a year visit the country. Most of these visitors come from other countries in the American continent, mainly <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>; followed by a growing number from the United States, Europe, and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> with a growing number of Asians from <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/PR_China" class="mw-redirect" title="PR China">PR China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main attractions for tourists are places of natural beauty situated in the extreme zones of the country: <a href="/wiki/San_Pedro_de_Atacama" title="San Pedro de Atacama">San Pedro de Atacama</a>, in the north, is very popular with foreign tourists who arrive to admire the Incaic architecture, the altiplano lakes, and the <a href="/wiki/Valle_de_la_Luna_(Chile)" title="Valle de la Luna (Chile)">Valley of the Moon</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In <a href="/wiki/Putre" title="Putre">Putre</a>, also in the north, there is the <a href="/wiki/Chungar%C3%A1_Lake" title="Chungará Lake">Chungará Lake</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Parinacota_Volcano" class="mw-redirect" title="Parinacota Volcano">Parinacota</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pomerape" title="Pomerape">Pomerape</a> volcanoes, with altitudes of 6,348 m and 6,282 m, respectively. Throughout the central Andes there are many ski resorts of international repute,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> including <a href="/wiki/Portillo,_Chile" title="Portillo, Chile">Portillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valle_Nevado" title="Valle Nevado">Valle Nevado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Termas_de_Chill%C3%A1n" title="Termas de Chillán">Termas de Chillán</a>.
</p><p>The main tourist sites in the south are national parks (the most popular is <a href="/wiki/Conguill%C3%ADo_National_Park" title="Conguillío National Park">Conguillío National Park</a> in the Araucanía)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the coastal area around Tirúa and Cañete with the <a href="/wiki/Isla_Mocha" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla Mocha">Isla Mocha</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nahuelbuta_National_Park" title="Nahuelbuta National Park">Nahuelbuta National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chilo%C3%A9_Archipelago" title="Chiloé Archipelago">Chiloé Archipelago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>, which includes <a href="/wiki/Laguna_San_Rafael_National_Park" title="Laguna San Rafael National Park">Laguna San Rafael National Park</a>, with its many glaciers, and the <a href="/wiki/Torres_del_Paine_National_Park" title="Torres del Paine National Park">Torres del Paine National Park</a>. The central port city of <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">Valparaíso</a>, which is World Heritage with its unique architecture, is also popular.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Finally, Easter Island in the Pacific Ocean is one of the main Chilean tourist destinations.
</p><p>For locals, tourism is concentrated mostly in the summer (December to March), and mainly in the coastal beach towns.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Arica" title="Arica">Arica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iquique" title="Iquique">Iquique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antofagasta" title="Antofagasta">Antofagasta</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Serena,_Chile" title="La Serena, Chile">La Serena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coquimbo" title="Coquimbo">Coquimbo</a> are the main summer centers in the north, and Pucón on the shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Villarrica" title="Lake Villarrica">Lake Villarrica</a> is the main center in the south. Because of its proximity to Santiago, the coast of the Valparaíso Region, with its many beach resorts, receives the largest number of tourists. <a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%B1a_del_Mar" title="Viña del Mar">Viña del Mar</a>, Valparaíso's northern affluent neighbor, is popular because of its beaches, <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casino</a>, and its annual <a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%B1a_del_Mar_International_Song_Festival" title="Viña del Mar International Song Festival">song festival</a>, the most important musical event in Latin America.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Pichilemu" title="Pichilemu">Pichilemu</a> in the <a href="/wiki/O%27Higgins_Region" title="O&#39;Higgins Region">O'Higgins Region</a> is widely known as South America's "best <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a> spot" according to <a href="/wiki/Fodor%27s" title="Fodor&#39;s">Fodor's</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In November 2005 the government launched a campaign under the brand "Chile: All Ways Surprising" intended to promote the country internationally for both business and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Chile" title="List of museums in Chile">Museums in Chile</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts" title="Chilean National Museum of Fine Arts">Chilean National Museum of Fine Arts</a> built in 1880, feature works by <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chilean_artists" title="List of Chilean artists">Chilean artists</a>.
</p><p>Chile is home to the world renowned <a href="/wiki/Patagonia_Park" title="Patagonia Park">Patagonian Trail</a> that resides on the border between Argentina and Chile. Chile recently launched a massive scenic route for tourism in hopes of encouraging development based on conservation. The Route of Parks covers 1,740 miles and was designed by Tompkin Conservation (founders <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Tompkins" title="Douglas Tompkins">Douglas Tompkins</a> and wife <a href="/wiki/Kristine_Tompkins" class="mw-redirect" title="Kristine Tompkins">Kristine</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Chile" title="Transport in Chile">Transport in Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mataveri_Airport_Easter_Island_Chile.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mataveri_Airport_Easter_Island_Chile.jpg/220px-Mataveri_Airport_Easter_Island_Chile.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mataveri_Airport_Easter_Island_Chile.jpg/330px-Mataveri_Airport_Easter_Island_Chile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mataveri_Airport_Easter_Island_Chile.jpg/440px-Mataveri_Airport_Easter_Island_Chile.jpg 2x" data-file-width="909" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mataveri_Airport_Easter_Island_Chile.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mataveri_International_Airport" title="Mataveri International Airport">Mataveri International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a></div></div></div>
<p>Due to Chile's topography a functioning transport network is vital to its economy. Buses are now the main means of long distance transportation in Chile, following the decline of its railway network.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The bus system covers the entire country, from <a href="/wiki/Arica,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Arica, Chile">Arica</a> to <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago, Chile">Santiago</a> (a 30-hour journey) and from Santiago to <a href="/wiki/Punta_Arenas" title="Punta Arenas">Punta Arenas</a> (about 40 hours, with a change at <a href="/wiki/Osorno,_Chile" title="Osorno, Chile">Osorno</a>).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CAF_en_Hernando_de_Magallanes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CAF_en_Hernando_de_Magallanes.jpg/220px-CAF_en_Hernando_de_Magallanes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CAF_en_Hernando_de_Magallanes.jpg/330px-CAF_en_Hernando_de_Magallanes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CAF_en_Hernando_de_Magallanes.jpg/440px-CAF_en_Hernando_de_Magallanes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CAF_en_Hernando_de_Magallanes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Santiago_Metro" title="Santiago Metro">Santiago Metro</a> is South America's most extensive metro system<sup id="cite_ref-Home_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Home-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Chile has a total of 372 runways (62 paved and 310 unpaved). Important airports in Chile include <a href="/wiki/Chacalluta_International_Airport" title="Chacalluta International Airport">Chacalluta International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Arica" title="Arica">Arica</a>), <a href="/wiki/Diego_Aracena_International_Airport" title="Diego Aracena International Airport">Diego Aracena International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Iquique" title="Iquique">Iquique</a>), <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Sabella_G%C3%A1lvez_International_Airport" title="Andrés Sabella Gálvez International Airport">Andrés Sabella Gálvez International Airport</a>
(<a href="/wiki/Antofagasta" title="Antofagasta">Antofagasta</a>), <a href="/wiki/Carriel_Sur_International_Airport" title="Carriel Sur International Airport">Carriel Sur International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n,_Chile" title="Concepción, Chile">Concepción</a>), <a href="/wiki/El_Tepual_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="El Tepual International Airport">El Tepual International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Puerto_Montt" title="Puerto Montt">Puerto Montt</a>), <a href="/wiki/Presidente_Carlos_Ib%C3%A1%C3%B1ez_del_Campo_International_Airport" title="Presidente Carlos Ibáñez del Campo International Airport">Presidente Carlos Ibáñez del Campo International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Punta_Arenas" title="Punta Arenas">Punta Arenas</a>), <a href="/wiki/La_Araucan%C3%ADa_International_Airport" title="La Araucanía International Airport">La Araucanía International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Temuco" title="Temuco">Temuco</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mataveri_International_Airport" title="Mataveri International Airport">Mataveri International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a>), the most remote airport in the world,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (February 2014)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Chile#Dubious" title="Talk:Chile">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Comodoro_Arturo_Merino_Ben%C3%ADtez_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Comodoro Arturo Merino Benítez International Airport">Comodoro Arturo Merino Benítez International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a>) with a traffic of 12,105,524 passengers in 2011. Santiago is headquarters of Latin America's largest <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a> <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> and Chilean <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/LAN_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="LAN Airlines">LAN Airlines</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andes_y_Torre_Entel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Andes_y_Torre_Entel.jpg/220px-Andes_y_Torre_Entel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Andes_y_Torre_Entel.jpg/330px-Andes_y_Torre_Entel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Andes_y_Torre_Entel.jpg/440px-Andes_y_Torre_Entel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="488" data-file-height="351" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andes_y_Torre_Entel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Torre_Entel" title="Torre Entel">Torre Entel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago de Chile">Santiago de Chile</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Andes_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Andes mountains">Andes mountains</a> in the background</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Chile" title="Telecommunications in Chile">Chile has a telecommunication</a> system which covers much of the country, including Chilean insular and Antarctic bases. Privatization of the telephone system began in 1988; Chile has one of the most advanced telecommunications infrastructure in South America with a modern system based on extensive microwave radio relay facilities and domestic satellite system with 3 earth stations.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, there were 3.276 million main lines in use and 24.13 million mobile cellular telephone subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> According to a 2012 database of the <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunications_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="International Telecommunications Union">International Telecommunications Union</a> (ITU), 61.42% of the Chilean population uses the internet, making Chile the country with the highest internet penetration in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ITU-IndividualsUsingTheInternet_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ITU-IndividualsUsingTheInternet-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The Chilean internet country code is "<a href="/wiki/.cl" title=".cl">.cl</a>".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Chile" title="Culture of Chile">Culture of Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Chile" title="Music of Chile">Music of Chile</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chilean_cuisine" title="Chilean cuisine">Chilean cuisine</a></div>
<p>From the period between early agricultural settlements and up to the late pre-Hispanic period, northern Chile was a region of Andean culture that was influenced by altiplano traditions spreading to the coastal valleys of the north, while southern regions were areas of Mapuche cultural activities. Throughout the colonial period following the conquest, and during the early Republican period, the country's culture was dominated by the Spanish. Other European influences, primarily English, French, and German began in the 19th century and have continued to this day. German migrants influenced the Bavarian style rural architecture and cuisine in the south of Chile in cities such as <a href="/wiki/Valdivia" title="Valdivia">Valdivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frutillar" title="Frutillar">Frutillar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Varas" title="Puerto Varas">Puerto Varas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osorno,_Chile" title="Osorno, Chile">Osorno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temuco" title="Temuco">Temuco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Octay" title="Puerto Octay">Puerto Octay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Llanquihue_Province" title="Llanquihue Province">Llanquihue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faja_Maisan" title="Faja Maisan">Faja Maisan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pitrufqu%C3%A9n" title="Pitrufquén">Pitrufquén</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Chile" title="Victoria, Chile">Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puc%C3%B3n" title="Pucón">Pucón</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Montt" title="Puerto Montt">Puerto Montt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zamacueca-Chile.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Zamacueca-Chile.jpg/220px-Zamacueca-Chile.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Zamacueca-Chile.jpg/330px-Zamacueca-Chile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Zamacueca-Chile.jpg/440px-Zamacueca-Chile.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1040" data-file-height="702" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zamacueca-Chile.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>La Zamacueca</i>, by Manuel Antonio Caro.</div></div></div>
<p>Music in Chile ranges from folkloric, popular and classical music. Its large geography generates different musical styles in the north, center and south of the country, including also Easter Island and Mapuche music.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The national dance is the <a href="/wiki/Cueca" title="Cueca">cueca</a>. Another form of traditional Chilean song, though not a dance, is the tonada. Arising from music imported by the Spanish colonists, it is distinguished from the cueca by an intermediate melodic section and a more prominent melody.
</p><p>Between 1950 and 1970 appears a rebirth in folk music leading by groups such as <a href="/wiki/Los_de_Ram%C3%B3n" title="Los de Ramón">Los de Ramón</a>, Los Cuatro Huasos and Los Huasos Quincheros, among others<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> with composers such as <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_de_Ram%C3%B3n" title="Raúl de Ramón">Raúl de Ramón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Violeta_Parra" title="Violeta Parra">Violeta Parra</a> and others. In the mid-1960s native musical forms were revitalized by the <a href="/wiki/Parra_family" title="Parra family">Parra family</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Nueva_canci%C3%B3n" title="Nueva canción">Nueva canción Chilena</a>, which was associated with political activists and reformers such as <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Jara" title="Víctor Jara">Víctor Jara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inti-Illimani" title="Inti-Illimani">Inti-Illimani</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quilapay%C3%BAn" title="Quilapayún">Quilapayún</a>. Other important <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a> singer and researcher on <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a> and Chilean <a href="/wiki/Ethnography" title="Ethnography">ethnography</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Margot_Loyola" title="Margot Loyola">Margot Loyola</a>. Also many Chilean rock bands like <a href="/wiki/Los_Jaivas" title="Los Jaivas">Los Jaivas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Prisioneros" title="Los Prisioneros">Los Prisioneros</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Ley_(band)" title="La Ley (band)">La Ley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Los_Tres" title="Los Tres">Los Tres</a> have reached international success. In February, annual music festivals are held in <a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%B1a_del_Mar" title="Viña del Mar">Viña del Mar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;max-width:227px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:117px;max-width:117px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Pablo_Neruda_1963.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Pablo Neruda" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Pablo_Neruda_1963.jpg/115px-Pablo_Neruda_1963.jpg" decoding="async" width="115" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Pablo_Neruda_1963.jpg/173px-Pablo_Neruda_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Pablo_Neruda_1963.jpg/230px-Pablo_Neruda_1963.jpg 2x" data-file-width="738" data-file-height="936" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:106px;max-width:106px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Gabriela_Mistral_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Gabriela Mistral" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gabriela_Mistral_1945.jpg/104px-Gabriela_Mistral_1945.jpg" decoding="async" width="104" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gabriela_Mistral_1945.jpg/156px-Gabriela_Mistral_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gabriela_Mistral_1945.jpg/208px-Gabriela_Mistral_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="280" data-file-height="396" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Pablo_Neruda" title="Pablo Neruda">Pablo Neruda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Mistral" title="Gabriela Mistral">Gabriela Mistral</a>, Nobel Prize recipients in literature</div></div></div></div>
<p>Chile is a <i>country of poets</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Mistral" title="Gabriela Mistral">Gabriela Mistral</a> was the first Latin American to receive a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> (1945). Chile's most famous poet is <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Neruda" title="Pablo Neruda">Pablo Neruda</a>, who received the Nobel Prize for Literature (1971) and is world-renowned for his extensive library of works on romance, nature, and politics. His three highly personalized homes in <a href="/wiki/Isla_Negra" title="Isla Negra">Isla Negra</a>, Santiago and Valparaíso are popular tourist destinations.
</p><p>Among the list of other Chilean poets are <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Pezoa_V%C3%A9liz" title="Carlos Pezoa Véliz">Carlos Pezoa Véliz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Huidobro" title="Vicente Huidobro">Vicente Huidobro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Rojas" title="Gonzalo Rojas">Gonzalo Rojas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_de_Rokha" title="Pablo de Rokha">Pablo de Rokha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicanor_Parra" title="Nicanor Parra">Nicanor Parra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Zurita" title="Raúl Zurita">Raúl Zurita</a>. <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Allende" title="Isabel Allende">Isabel Allende</a> is the best-selling Chilean novelist, with 51 millions of her novels sold worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Novelist <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Donoso" title="José Donoso">José Donoso</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Obscene_Bird_of_Night" title="The Obscene Bird of Night">The Obscene Bird of Night</a></i> is considered by critic <a href="/wiki/Harold_Bloom" title="Harold Bloom">Harold Bloom</a> to be one of the canonical works of 20th-century Western literature. Another internationally recognized Chilean novelist and poet is <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Bola%C3%B1o" title="Roberto Bolaño">Roberto Bolaño</a> whose translations into English have had an excellent reception from the critics.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Asado_chileno_-_Flickr_-_Marieloreto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Asado_chileno_-_Flickr_-_Marieloreto.jpg/220px-Asado_chileno_-_Flickr_-_Marieloreto.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Asado_chileno_-_Flickr_-_Marieloreto.jpg/330px-Asado_chileno_-_Flickr_-_Marieloreto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Asado_chileno_-_Flickr_-_Marieloreto.jpg/440px-Asado_chileno_-_Flickr_-_Marieloreto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Asado_chileno_-_Flickr_-_Marieloreto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chilean <i><a href="/wiki/Asado" title="Asado">Asado</a></i> (Barbecue) and <i><a href="/wiki/Marraqueta" title="Marraqueta">Marraqueta</a></i></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chilean_cuisine" title="Chilean cuisine">Chilean cuisine</a> is a reflection of the country's topographical variety, featuring an assortment of seafood, beef, fruits, and vegetables. Traditional recipes include <a href="/wiki/Asado" title="Asado">asado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cazuela" title="Cazuela">cazuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Empanada" title="Empanada">empanadas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humita" title="Humita">humitas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pastel_de_choclo" title="Pastel de choclo">pastel de choclo</a>, pastel de papas, <a href="/wiki/Curanto" title="Curanto">curanto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sopaipilla#Chile" title="Sopaipilla">sopaipillas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crudos" title="Crudos">Crudos</a> is an example of the mixture of culinary contributions from the various ethnic influences in Chile. The raw minced <a href="/wiki/Llama" title="Llama">llama</a>, heavy use of shellfish and rice bread were taken from native <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Quechua</a> Andean cuisine, (although now beef brought to Chile by Europeans is also used in place of the llama meat), lemon and onions were brought by the Spanish colonists, and the use of <a href="/wiki/Mayonnaise" title="Mayonnaise">mayonnaise</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a> was introduced by German immigrants, as was <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folklore">Folklore</span></h3>
<p>The folklore of Chile, cultural and demographic characteristics of the country, is the result of mixture of Spanish and Amerindian elements that occurred during the colonial period. Due to cultural and historical reasons, they are classified and distinguished four major areas in the country: northern areas, central, southern and south. Most of the traditions of the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Chile" title="Culture of Chile">culture of Chile</a> have a festive purpose, but some, such as dances and ceremonies, have religious components.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mythology">Mythology</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chilean_mythology" title="Chilean mythology">Chilean mythology</a></div>
<p>Chilean mythology is the mythology and beliefs of the Folklore of Chile.
</p><p>This includes <a href="/wiki/Chilote_mythology" title="Chilote mythology">Chilote mythology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui_mythology" title="Rapa Nui mythology">Rapa Nui mythology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mapuche_mythology" class="mw-redirect" title="Mapuche mythology">Mapuche mythology</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Chile" title="Cinema of Chile">Cinema of Chile</a></div>
<p>Film production originated in <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">Valparaíso</a> on 26 May 1902 with the premiere of the documentary <i>Exercise General Fire Brigade</i>, the first film completely filmed and processed in the country. In the following decades, marked milestones <i>The deck of Death</i> (or <i>The Enigma of Lord Street</i>) (1916), considered the first film of a Chilean story, <i>The transmission of presidential</i> (1920), the first animated film in the country, and <i>North and South</i> (1934), the first sound film of Chile.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Chile" title="Sport in Chile">Sport in Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Nacional_de_Chile_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estadio_Nacional_de_Chile_2.jpg/220px-Estadio_Nacional_de_Chile_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estadio_Nacional_de_Chile_2.jpg/330px-Estadio_Nacional_de_Chile_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estadio_Nacional_de_Chile_2.jpg/440px-Estadio_Nacional_de_Chile_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1750" data-file-height="1137" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Nacional_de_Chile_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Nacional_Julio_Mart%C3%ADnez_Pr%C3%A1danos" title="Estadio Nacional Julio Martínez Prádanos">Estadio Nacional Julio Martínez Prádanos</a></div></div></div>
<p>Chile's most popular sport is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>. Chile has appeared in nine FIFA World Cups which includes hosting the <a href="/wiki/1962_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1962 FIFA World Cup">1962 FIFA World Cup</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_football_team" title="Chile national football team">national football team</a> finished third. Other results achieved by the national football team include two <a href="/wiki/Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Copa América">Copa América</a> titles (<a href="/wiki/2015_Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="2015 Copa América">2015</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copa_Am%C3%A9rica_Centenario" title="Copa América Centenario">2016</a>), and two runners up positions,  one silver and two bronze medals at the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>, a bronze medal at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Summer Olympics</a> and two third places finishes in the FIFA under-17 and under-20 youth tournaments. The top league in the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_football_league_system" title="Chilean football league system">Chilean football league system</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Chilean Primera División">Chilean Primera División</a>, which is named by the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Football_History_%26_Statistics" title="International Federation of Football History &amp; Statistics">IFFHS</a> as the ninth strongest national football league in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-iffhs_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iffhs-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main football clubs are <a href="/wiki/Colo-Colo" title="Colo-Colo">Colo-Colo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Club_Universidad_de_Chile" title="Club Universidad de Chile">Universidad de Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Universidad_Cat%C3%B3lica" title="Club Deportivo Universidad Católica">Universidad Católica</a>. Colo-Colo is the country's most successful football club, having both the most national and international championships, including the coveted <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> South American club tournament. Universidad de Chile was the last international champion (<a href="/wiki/Copa_Sudamericana" title="Copa Sudamericana">Copa Sudamericana</a> 2011).
</p><p>Tennis is Chile's most successful sport. Its <a href="/wiki/Chile_Davis_Cup_team" title="Chile Davis Cup team">national team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/World_Team_Cup" title="World Team Cup">World Team Cup</a> clay tournament twice (2003 &amp; 2004), and played the <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a> final against <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> in 1976. At the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a> the country captured gold and bronze in men's singles and gold in men's doubles. <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_R%C3%ADos" title="Marcelo Ríos">Marcelo Ríos</a> became the first Latin American man to reach the number one spot in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_ATP_number_1_ranked_players" class="mw-redirect" title="List of ATP number 1 ranked players">ATP singles rankings</a> in 1998. <a href="/wiki/Anita_Lizana" title="Anita Lizana">Anita Lizana</a> won the <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a> in 1937, becoming the first woman from Latin America to win a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tournament. <a href="/wiki/Luis_Ayala_(tennis)" title="Luis Ayala (tennis)">Luis Ayala</a> was twice a runner-up at the French Open and both Ríos and <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Fernando González">Fernando González</a> reached the Australian Open men's singles finals. González also won a silver medal in singles at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> in Beijing.
</p><p>At the Summer Olympic Games Chile boasts a total of two gold medals (tennis), seven silver medals (athletics, <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Equestrian at the Summer Olympics">equestrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, shooting and tennis) and four bronze medals (tennis, boxing and football). In 2012, Chile won its first Paralympic Games medal (gold in Athletics).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15_Abril_2015,_Ministro_%C3%81lvaro_Elizalde_junto_a_la_Presidenta_Michelle_Bachelet_reciben_al_Equipo_Campe%C3%B3n_Mundial_de_Polo_en_La_Moneda._(17160926755).jpg" class="image"><img srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/15_Abril_2015%2C_Ministro_%C3%81lvaro_Elizalde_junto_a_la_Presidenta_Michelle_Bachelet_reciben_al_Equipo_Campe%C3%B3n_Mundial_de_Polo_en_La_Moneda._%2817160926755%29.jpg/330px-15_Abril_2015%2C_Ministro_%C3%81lvaro_Elizalde_junto_a_la_Presidenta_Michelle_Bachelet_reciben_al_Equipo_Campe%C3%B3n_Mundial_de_Polo_en_La_Moneda._%2817160926755%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1669" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15_Abril_2015,_Ministro_%C3%81lvaro_Elizalde_junto_a_la_Presidenta_Michelle_Bachelet_reciben_al_Equipo_Campe%C3%B3n_Mundial_de_Polo_en_La_Moneda._(17160926755).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Chilean national polo team with President <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet" title="Michelle Bachelet">Michelle Bachelet</a> and the trophy of the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Polo_Championship" title="2015 World Polo Championship">2015 World Polo Championship</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chilean_rodeo" title="Chilean rodeo">Rodeo</a> is the country's <a href="/wiki/National_sport" title="National sport">national sport</a> and is practiced in the more rural areas of the nation. A sport similar to <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Chueca" title="Chueca">chueca</a></i> was played by the Mapuche people during the Spanish conquest. <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">Skiing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snowboarding" title="Snowboarding">snowboarding</a> are practiced at ski centers located in the Central Andes, and in southern ski centers near to cities as Osorno, Puerto Varas, Temuco and Punta Arenas. <a href="/wiki/Surfing_in_Chile" title="Surfing in Chile">surfing</a> is popular at some coastal towns. <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">Polo</a> is professionally practiced within Chile, with the country achieving top prize in the 2008 and 2015 <a href="/wiki/World_Polo_Championship" title="World Polo Championship">World Polo Championship</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a> is a popular sport in which Chile has earned a bronze medal in the first men's <a href="/wiki/FIBA_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA World Championship">FIBA World Championship</a> held in 1950 and winning a second bronze medal when Chile hosted the <a href="/wiki/1959_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1959 FIBA World Championship">1959 FIBA World Championship</a>. Chile hosted the first <a href="/wiki/FIBA_World_Championship_for_Women" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA World Championship for Women">FIBA World Championship for Women</a> in 1953 finishing the tournament with the silver medal. <a href="/wiki/San_Pedro_de_Atacama" title="San Pedro de Atacama">San Pedro de Atacama</a> is host to the annual "Atacama Crossing", a six-stage, 250-kilometre (160&#160;mi) footrace which annually attracts about 150 competitors from 35 countries. The <a href="/wiki/Dakar_Rally" title="Dakar Rally">Dakar Rally</a> <a href="/wiki/Off-road_racing" title="Off-road racing">off-road automobile race</a> has been held in both Chile and <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> since 2009.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_heritage">Cultural heritage</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">cultural heritage</a> of Chile consists, first, of their intangible heritage, composed of various cultural events, such as visual arts, crafts, dances, holidays, cuisine, games, music and traditions, and, secondly, by its tangible, consists of those buildings, objects and sites of archaeological, architectural, traditional, artistic, ethnographic, folkloric, historical, religious or technological scattered through Chilean territory, among them, those goods are declared <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, in accordance with the provisions of the Convention concerning the Protection of World Cultural and Natural Heritage of 1972, ratified by Chile in 1980. These cultural sites are the <a href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui_National_Park" title="Rapa Nui National Park">Rapa Nui National Park</a> (1995), the <a href="/wiki/Churches_of_Chilo%C3%A9" title="Churches of Chiloé">Churches of Chiloé</a> (2000), <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">the historical district of the port city of Valparaíso</a> (2003), <a href="/wiki/Humberstone_and_Santa_Laura_Saltpeter_Works" title="Humberstone and Santa Laura Saltpeter Works">Humberstone and Santa Laura Saltpeter Works</a> (2005) and the mining city <a href="/wiki/Sewell,_Chile" title="Sewell, Chile">Sewell</a> (2006).
</p><p>In 1999 the <i>Cultural Heritage Day</i> was established as a way to honour and commemorate Chiles cultural heritage. It is an official national event celebrated in May every year.
</p>

<li>Brian Lovemen, <i>Chile: The Legacy of Hispanic Capitalism</i>, 3rd ed., Oxford University Press, 2001</li>
<li>John L. Rector, <i>The History of Chile</i>, Greenwood Press, 2003</li>
<li>Christian Balteum: <i>The Strip. A marxist critique of a semicomparador economy</i>, University of Vermont Press, 2018</li></ul>
